O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	For you, dear children, I have completed this book which is the conclusion of the art of medicine, and have ended it through its explanations and by making its statements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And I was shown in my vision that I would complete it with this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is practiced in our region and has been removed everywhere, it has lost its science and has been stripped down, and nothing remains from what was outside except for the small descriptions in books by ancient times that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And thus error and vanity have arisen, and minds are closed, and the science has been distanced away.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	It seems to me that I should revive this treatise together with the order of this medical text according to the way of exposition and disclosure and abbreviation; and will come together with the forms of iron cautery tools, and other working instruments along with the adjustment of their declaration and preparation, exactly as it is necessary.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because there are no skilled doctors to be found in our time, the art of medicine has become lost.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for the one who intervenes to master anatomy science as Galen says, so long as they know how to judge the members, their forms and connections, separations of tendons, and have knowledge about bones, nerves and sinews, including the number of bones, their arrangement and movement, as well as the veins that move and those that are stationary, and understand where their outlets are.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And it was stated by Hippocrates that not with nothing but with something is much, and not with one but with many in the art of hands.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We will tell you at the beginning of this book that if someone does not understand what has been said before, they might make mistakes and deceive people; just as I have seen many times in those who interfere with this knowledge and abandon their studies.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I saw a fool who cauterized one of the lymph nodes or neck of a woman, and burned the blood vessels in her neck; because so much blood came out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And I saw another barber who treated a stone in an old man's kidney, and the stone was large; so he carried away with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died after three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have already been called to draw out this, and see the condition of the patient and the size of the stone, and indeed if it was cut for him he would die.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another case where I treated a duke of our land who had his leg broken, and along with the breaking there was an injury. And these doctors full of ignorance allowed the breaking to occur over the injury as though it were healed by strong luck, and did not drain at all from the injury; and left him like that for one month; and commanded him not to disturb it again; and waited thus until his leg was completely swollen and his toes and suffered destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I have been called to come to him, and I hurried to come to relieve his leg; and when I heard that it was relieved so smoothly and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every pathway of corruption had already been confirmed or within the body and could not be cured; and the process of decay continued throughout the body as long as the limbs were completely lost.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see one other place where an abscess was flattened out, and then it swelled up due to the wickedness of its lordess.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For a boil, when it is filled with melancholic humor, it should not be touched by iron if it isn't in such a position that one can remove all the corrupted parts.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, dear children, you need to know that the work of hands is divided into two parts: meaning, the task where there is danger in multiple conditions; and I will show you within each part of this book where it has risk and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos.	Because it is necessary for you to remember this, so that others do not speak ill of you.
Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you take your weapons in caution, and treat your illnesses lightly yet firmly, and use the best path so that through the grace of God you come to salvation and become fortunate; and leave the terrifying diseases without complaint for healing; and remove from yourself those who make you doubt, and have faith in yourselves so that you can come from this world to glory on the other side.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.»	Galen states in some of his admonishments: "Do not take any illness as bad, lest you be called a foolish one by others."
J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc .iij. chapitres.	I have written this treatise according to three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire cauteries and medicinal cauteries, and the chapters are arranged from head to stone; and about the forms of instruments, and the metals of cautery, and all that is necessary for the operation.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapters are about cutting and piercing, and suction cups and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapters are arranged and discuss the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is arranged from head to stone, and discusses the forms of instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Just as we recall our work, it is necessary that I describe the quality of each remedy and its harm for each constitution.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I state that the qualities of aid, and harm, are the longest word and most subtle science and secrets they respond to. And many wise people spoke about this, agreeing with it; and they barely allow me to understand them because I fear their lengthiness.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery is universally applicable to all constitutions where there is matter, for there are two constitutions: namely, a warm constitution with matter, and a dry constitution with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In the warm and dry combined constitutions with matter, they devised something and said that the fire cautery is great help; and another group said the opposite: that the fire cautery only works for diseases originating from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is so hot and should not be treated with hot diseases by heat or drying. And this man who says otherwise, that the cautery provides great help to hot and dry illnesses that come into bodies.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of the person and their moisture to the constitution of fire, you find that the body is cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have found it true on every occasion through experimentation.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And every way, do not interfere with it except the one who has proven it, and who knows through long usage the art of cautery, and the variety of human complexion, and the dispositions and causes of their illnesses, and the occurrences and space during treatment; we have no fear from other complexions, especially in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all these things gathered together and agreed with the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that a combined fire cautery has secrets of healing and offers greater benefit than a burning medicine cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and does not come forth from any other member except the one being cooked, and it harms no other limb if you do not name it.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide.	The burning medicines spread from one member to another by removing, and bring diseases of injury healing; and by chance the patient gets the ailment.
Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire due to its height and due to the goodness of its substance does not cause this unless there is excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this through experience and the length of service and study that I've put into the art, which aligns with the truth of things; and because of this, I apologize for the length of my words, as I do not wish to withhold the secret of fire or the quality of its work, how it relieves diseases from the body, just as the philosopher explains in demonstrating. May you receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, child, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be performed, and studied prayers.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is suitable in all times, for the nuisances occurring are reduced by the aid of the fire cautery; and also if the cauterizations are for necessary pains that cannot wait until a greater evil befalls the limb.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And never think, foolish child, like those who misunderstand; for a disease cured by cauterization has no return. And they say it this way: but it is not as they believe, because cauterizations are merely medicine that alters the complexion and dries up fluids which cause pain, and is worth more than medicine due to its speed in enhancing strength, and due to the virtue of its work and its sovereignty.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And know that disease can come at any time according to the constitution of the body and the nature of the illness and its virtue; and they are gathered in him the superfluities due to the intake of food and similar things, unless cauterization is given when there is little excess and moisture, such as with cauterizations for pain, and similar matters, so that this kind of pain does not recur; but it happens rarely.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And very few people understand why cauterization is called the last resort of medicine, and it's clear to see; but they don't believe that cauterization can be effective after medicine. But their understanding is false, as cauterization is the last resort in medicine because when our methods for cures do not work in any disease, then we administer our cauterizer, and it works.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, it's true that cauterization is the last resort of medicine, not according to the understanding of others who misunderstand.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The old ones said that gold cauterizing tools are better than those made of iron, and they mentioned this only because of the quality of gold and the high status of its substance; and they stated that gold cautery blades do not cause infection, but that is not visible since I have experienced it myself, and found out that it can indeed cause infection in some individuals; and gold cauterizing tools are better than iron ones, as they declared.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And still, when you heat the gold instrument, you do not realize it by the color of the gold, and it gets instantly cooled off; and if it is heated too much; then put it in fire; and thus there should be enough prevention.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this, we use our metal cautery that we have adapted to our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	So you should order this chapter about the shoulder until it reaches the elbow, for the sake of making it easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive cauterizer
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	A cautery is useful against moisture and cold near the head. There are two of these that we perform due to the cause of an illness called 'soda', and through the influence of many humors descending from the eyes, ears, and through a multitude of dreams, toothache, throat pain, and especially for all diseases coming from cold such as paralysis, soda poisoning, apoplexy, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The shape of this cautery is such that the patient's body is purged by dissolving medicine, modifying the head three times or four times, depending on how the virtues and heat and custom to which the patient can withstand it; then wash the head with the dissolved medicine.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	Then place their hands together between your palms and place your hands on the tip of his nose. After placing the root of your palm against the root of his nose between his two nostrils; and when your middle fingers reach, if it bleeds through, then warm the cautery called "olivare", which has this form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place it in its original location with ink, and as you lower and adjust your hand little by little while turning it around; then lift your hand alone, and check the bone if you see a small dot of .i. sol; and if you don't see it, continue using the cautery until you see the bone as I have told you; afterwards take .i. poc of flour, and place damp cotton inside, and apply it to the site, and leave it there for .iij. days; after that put on a moist cream in butter; and leave it on until the scab is removed; afterwards treat the wound with ointment called 'tetrafarmaçon', until it heals.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And if someone said that when a wound remains open longer, the more it purges out pus; and for this reason, movement is advised.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they said that one should leave the cautery for so long that part of the bone is burned, and then restart with what has been burned by the bone, and treat it.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And it says that for the fire cautery, one should let it remain there and press so hard that you lift as wide as two small cones like those women place in their bellies because fluids are forced out; and should one leave the wound open for a long time; after this, one must clean and bind it.
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterization do not seem to me to be good for everything, except when there is a flow of fear; and I think that I should leave them. For the limbs are weakened by continuous discharge from nature as we have shown in other members; and even when the limb of disease is weak by nature, and my first sign of cauterization is more saved and healed to me, and I use this method generally thus assemble health.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old pain in the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When throughout the whole head comes chronic pain and lasts long, then one should use the patient's herbs and pills that are called "cochie", and treatments for clearing the head and ears and bandages; and if one applies to them the cautery as we have said before, and it proves beneficial.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the patient's head is of strong nature and not too cold; then apply the cautery over the spot where we have spoken above for a moment.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After make the cautery on each horn of the head up to the bone, as we have said before, and do one more cautery at the place that is called "vasselz"; and use two leu's in which you put suction cups; and ease your hand so that you don't touch until the bone: the patient feels much greater pain in this cautery compared to others, and I will speak of it elsewhere; and it should be known that the cauteries on the horns are more delicate than those done for half the middle of the head, and this is their shape.
dou cautere dou chief	Of the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hair grow long and even; and if they pierce at their base, hold them steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When sudden pain occurs in part of the head, and the disease extends up to the eye, and the head is cleansed by purifying medicines, and various other treatments that I mentioned in the division of diseases were performed, but none helped: then he should apply cautery according to two methods, namely using an ague medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The application of the ague medicine cautery involves taking one spoonful of oil and applying it with a bandage to two parts of each head, in such a way that you can place the spoonful of oil on the skin; then press and hold well for about 12 hours, and then release and remove the garlic. Leave the wound like this for 2 days or 3. Then apply a poultice with butter until pain disappears.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the oil treatment as long as it's clean; and if you see that you should use some of those burning medicines I have written or in the tenth treatise on burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere. Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	The iron cautery is done like this way. Heat up the form of the iron that is as follows:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait .i. poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it "clos" because the head is made in the shape of a bell where it has .i. point of curvature, and in the middle there's a small appearance; and place it on the painful area, and hold your hand and gently move the iron for a bit, until half of the thickness of the wound is burned; then lift your hand to prevent the artery from burning, allowing blood flow, and apply an abundance of bleeding.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par .iij. jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After that, put cotton in the wound as a bandage and keep it on for three days; then replace with damp cotton soaked in butter, and continue treating the wound with oil until it is clean. If you wish to cauterize this headache with the iron cautery which is called 'cultellare', do so at its entire point, but beware not to cover the artery in this headache as it is not old.
de emigraine	Of migraine
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	When you treat migraine as we have discussed in the divisions of diseases before, and if there is no improvement, and you see that the cauteries previously mentioned in medicine do not suit it, then you must heat the cautery called "cultellare" until it is white; and do this by placing it along the limb where a line halfway between half an inch and one inch long, and hold your hand steady once, and pull gently so as not to cut the artery and stop when reaching the bone; and watch out for the jaw that closes when eating, make sure only the mouth moves and no spasms affect the patient, and be cautious of bleeding from the artery if it is cut, or cutting too much and similarly for those who are inexperienced and untested; leave the work halfway done, but I will tell you how to stop bleeding once the artery has been cut, and show you its proper place in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait .ij. coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauteries do not suit the illness and the patient is suffering, apply them to the middle of the head as we have said, and treat the wound until it heals; and when you notice this, administer the cauterizing instrument that we've mentioned in the chapter on extraction of arteries with a two-edged cauterizer; and these are better than others and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	of the pain of the ear from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When pain from cold comes to the ear, and there have been operations with dissolving medicines and other treatments we mentioned in this division, if the pain does not subside, then heat this cautery called 'pints', as shown here:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les .ij. se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait .x. poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying the cautery to all around the ear, or around both of them where the pain is held in, remove it slightly from the root of the ear after you have indicated its place. Place ten pints around each ear; treat the area until it becomes healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torment of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	Pain that should be treated with a cautery does not include those that move by flemmings, as we have stated in the divisions of diseases; and no cautery should be done on symptoms that come from dryness and pus of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de .iij. cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des .ij. levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you treat this instance of pain that moves by flemmings from water and the purging of head and gargling, and when it fails, then it should be that you apply the heat of .iij. cauteries: one at the root of the ear, and another a little further on the temple, and the third in fitting the .ij. lips; and put the cautery where health opens up, and make it cauterize the area above the ear near a bit under the horn of the head, and another on the temple as long as an inch; and let the cautery burn there until half of the flesh is burned; and this is the shape of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And there is the appearance of surgical pain as we placed before, but it's a bit more subtle; you should have the knife slightly larger; after treating the limb as I said previously, until it becomes healthy.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai .iiij. cauteres: .ij. sus les .ij. cornes dou chief, et .i. emmi le chief, et .i. ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When dealing with an old apoplexy and treating it as we have said, if the patient does not benefit, and the sick has fever, then do this: four cauterizations: two on each of the two horns above the head, and one underneath the head, and one in the region known as 'vasselz' as previously mentioned. Lastly, perform a cautery near the mouth of the stomach; and treat it similarly to how we have said before.
de litargie	of liturgy
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this illness, you should give the patient large pills and medicines that facilitate the brain's function; after that, let the doctor remove everything on top of the patient's head, and then apply the sulfur plaster to the back part of the head. And here is how to perform a cautery: do it as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai .iij. cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere .i. doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai .i. cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, .ij. autres sus les .ij. cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it's healed like this, that's good; and if not, do the following: three times apply a heat on descending from the head to the collarbone, leaving an interval of about two fingers between each application; treat as with others. If you see the need for adjustment after doing so and there is pain in the flesh, apply one heat in the middle. If further treatment is needed, do it twice more on both sides until it's healed; and use the heats known as "olive-shaped", as I've mentioned before.
de la froidor dou chief	from cold of the head
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et .i. derrier et .iij. sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai .iiij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	It is necessary that the head be cleaned of old scabs and what we have previously mentioned. After rubbing the head with a warm compress, then apply heat to the flesh, and on each horn of the head, and twice behind and three times on the spine below the collarbone; if you need more treatment and the area is moist and there's pain, and the illness persists, then apply four heats on the spine of the back. Let it sit until the most tender part is well dried, then lift your hand; after this, treat it until healed, and use the heat method known as "olive-shaped", as we have mentioned before.
de l’epilempsie	Of the cautery
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	The epileptics should only use a cautery for those who are phlegmatic, and it is necessary to first modify the brain with years of other treatments that we have mentioned in the section where the sick body is large and suffers from lack of medicine.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai .i. cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et .i. cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is a child who cannot endure this treatment, make them gargle and chew often with good meats; after that they take their head in the middle, and I do as I have said for one dose of cautery, and another on the vein, and on each horn; and if the body is large and suffering, make them receive cauterizations like what I have told about those who are paralyzed and have softening of limbs, on the spinal column in back and neck, and let the olive wood cauterization be as I have said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai .i. cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	And if the body is a child, make one delicate cautery according to this manner:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When due to the cause of melancholy are excesses or fluids corrupted and large phlegm, then apply the partial cautery we have described to those who suffer from paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if due to the cause of melancholy are the excesses declining into melancholy and is there moisture in the body that affects the skin, then let him drink something so that the brain may be cleansed, as was described before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai .i. torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com .i. cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After obtaining the lymph from the body; afterwards make one and a half lin thread well made, as one circle, place it inside the lymph; and if there are any irregularities in the lymph, ensure they settle down and maintain proper support from all sides; after that present the liniment, mix it with old burberry butter; and heat it over fire until it can be tolerated by those who might be susceptible to heat; afterwards remove the circle through its opening while inside the body, and let it cool down; and do this once every week for a lymph each time with another good administration, until they are well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere. Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	If you see that the person is being cauterized by making several points across the whole area of the cautery. This method moistens the brain greatly; and then place wet cotton, butter, and gelatin fat on it.
de l’awe des eulz	of the fear of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When fear comes first for the eyes due to the symptoms I have mentioned in the division, then begin and continue to make the patient consume something that purifies the head, keeps him away from all moisture, and makes him sweat or take baths several times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as .ij. eulz ensamble, ou en .i. se li dessendemens est en .i.; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After he commands about his head and makes him cauterize it, and makes two cauterizations on the two temples where his fear begins to descend along with the fear of both eyes together, or when his fear descends in one eye; and treat all the cauterizations for all the veins and arteries that are around the brain, and make them cauterize long according to the width of the temple; and beware of blood clotting, and if you see too much blood coming out, then stop it with a piece as you can.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les .ij. os derrier.	And I will teach you about the extraction of arteries and incisions using the cautery, how to apply it; and one should never perform a cautery or cauterize between the two bones behind.
dou cors des larmes	of the two paths of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: .i. cautere emmi le chief, et .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. temples, et .ij. cauteres ou haiterel desoz les .ij. os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout .i. petit cautere.	When the tears of the eyes are old and accustomed, and located on the veins, or beneath the arteries that are visible underneath the surface at the forehead; and one sees that they result from excesses of cold humors, then apply the cautery as I have said at the beginning of this discussion: .i. on the forehead, and .ij. cauterizations above the two temples, and .ij. cauterizations or cauterize below the two bones; and if more is needed, carefully cauterize just above the eyebrows with every .i small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	of the inner paths of tears through the eyes
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide .iij. nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai .ij. cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les .ij. sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you apply the medicine according to what we have said in the division, and it doesn't benefit, then give the patient three nuts to drink; after this, put your hand on their head and apply a cautery or an olive oil-based balm; and do two more applications of the same cautery known as 'clavilis' on the two ears, a little over the hair. And guard yourself not to cover the artery.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cautery which is called 'clavilis':
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare». de coi ci est li forme:	When the paper of the oil is softened due to illness and moisture, then apply this type of cautery which is called 'olivare'. Here's its form:
Et se tu vues si fai .ij. cauteres sus les .ij. sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you see to do two cauterizations on the two nostrils as long as they are together; and don't let your hand rest until a third part of the paper is burnt, following the method I have described.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of hair that touches the eye
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc .ij. manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	None of the times has it happened that the hair of the nostrils turns into the gum and touches the eye, in which case one performs cauterization according to two methods: namely by fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant il naissent et i sont igalz, adonques met le malaide en ton sain; aprés seigne sus la papiere des eulz une figure que soit ausi com li fuelle dou mirte, et soit li comencemens dou signe delez les poilz; puis i met coton moilliet en glaire d’uef et muscillaige de persillion sus l’oil, puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When they are born and evenly long, then instruct the patient to be in good health; afterward depict on paper a figure that resembles a leaf of myrtle, with the beginning of the sign below the hairs. Then place moistened cotton in egg white glaze and cloves beneath the eye, then apply heat from this fire which has been shaped accordingly:
Aprés cauterize sus la figure que tu as signiet poc et poc mout de fois, que li keurs soit ars lai endroit; et li signes de la santeit de l’uevre est que tu voies la papiere retraite, et les poilz levez a la pointure de l’oil; adonques lieve ta main, et laisse ensi .iij. jors, puis i met coton moilliet en burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Afterwards cauterize on the figure you have drawn little by little a few times, until the burns are located in that place; and the signs of health from the work is that you see the paper pulled back, and the hairs raised to the point of the eye; then lift your hand, and leave like this for three days, then place moistened cotton in butter until the scorching is removed; afterwards apply ointment until it heals properly.
Et se aprés ceu vienent li poilz, et li papiere est mollifie adonques rencomence le cautere sus cel leu meisme, si com tu as fait premiers; et se li poil sont defuer, si le cauterize tant que li papiere soit levee a son leu natureil, et soit igals, et ne poignent mie li poil l’oil.	And if after this the hairs come out, and the paper becomes soft, then restart the cautery on that same place as you did first; and if the hairs are gone, cauterize until the paper is raised to its natural level, and evenly so, and does not pinch the eye.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient grans et igalz, puis fai de parchemin la forme de la foille de mirte; puis pren de savon fransois et de vive chalz, de chescun une .З., et broie ensamble bien; et le fai hastanment, si qu’il ne refroide, puis en espant sus la forme que tu es fait sicom la foille dou mirte, et met sus la papiere des eulz; et se li maladie tient en .i. oil soulement, si doit on ovrer en .i., et se en ambedous ausi; et met desoz l’oil coton moilliet en abin d’uef; et li chiés dou malaide soit en ton sain et met ton doi mostrant sus la medicine, et presse .i. poc et lou muef toutes les fois que li malaide sent mordication de la medicine, car il sent mordication ausi com de feu.	The hot medical cautery requires that the patient allow their hairs to grow long and evenly; then make a form of the bay leaf out of parchment. Then take French soap and fresh garlic from each, one unit each, grind them together finely; and do it quickly so it doesn't cool down, then spread it on the form like a bay leaf and place it on paper under the eyes. If the illness lasts only in one oil, you must open just that one, and if also in both; and put moistened cotton next to the oil as in an egg; and the patient's head be under your healthy hand with your thumb showing over the medicine, press once every time the patient senses the medicine's bite because they sense the bite similarly to fire.
Quant tu as ceu fait longement, si oste la medicine a ton doit.	When you have done this for a while, then apply the medicine to your finger.
Et quant li mordication sera passee, si leve le leu d’awe, et rewarde se tu vois la papiere levee ausi com s’ele estoit levee par constraignement de feu ou par incision; et s’il est ensi, si est bien. Se ceu non, si remet encor de la medicine sus lou leu ou li medicine n’ait ovreit, tant que tes ovraiges soit igalz, et tes eulz mis a point; puis met sus coton moilliet en burre tant que li keurs ars soit cheus, aprés cure le leu de l’oignement qui est apelez «dyafenis» et d’autre, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the biting has passed, then lift your finger away from it. If you see the paper lifted as if it had been lifted by fire or incision; and if so is the case, then it's well. Should this not be the case, reapply the medicine to your finger until all of your actions are equal and your eyes set right; then place moistened cotton in butter until your knuckles are burnt, after that treat your finger with the ointment called "dyafenis" and another, until it becomes healthy.
Et se t’est mestier que tu te warde bien a ton ovraige par grant warde qu’il ne chiece point de la medicine as eulz.  Et se li papiere devient mole aprés, et li poil poignent en l’oil, si recomence la medicine sus celui leu qui est mollifiez de la papiere proprement, ensi com tu as fait devant; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme de la fuelle dou mirte:	And if it is necessary that you protect yourself well in your work by great caution so that no part of the medicine affects this. And if the paper becomes damp after, and the hair pinches into the eye, then repeat the medicine on that area which has been softened by the proper paper; just as you did before; after that it is cured until it is sane; and this is the form of the leaf of mire:
Et saichés que li eul des homes sont divers en grandor et en petitece, et selonc ceu soit tes constraignemens; et ne soit mie reponue li droite voie a celui cui est li estude de cest art.	And know that the hair of men is diverse in size and smallness, and according to this be your constraints; and do not let the right way answer to him who studies this art.
de la cure de fistule par cautere	of the treatment of fistula by cautery
Quant tu cures fistule si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladies, et tes cures ne profitent mie, adonques covient il que tu li fais cautere selonc ceste maniere.	When you are treating a fistula as we have said in the divisions of diseases, and your treatments do not benefit, then it is necessary that you apply the cautery method like this.
Comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain; et teigne li menistres son chief entre tes mains en teil maniere qu’il ne se mueve, ne ne demoinne son chief; aprés met coton moilliet en abin d’uef ou en jus de persillion sus l’oil; aprés chaufe le cautere qui est teilz: et est chevez au chief si com li forme d’une penne de vouteul, ensamble la queil soit li cautere; se tu vues, si soit apointé des l’un chief dusc’a l’autre, et se tu vues, si soit ausi com une tente; mais toutevoie, cist qui est chevez vaut mues por ton ovraige.	Instruct the patient to place their head in your healthy position; and hold the eyes of the head between your hands so that it doesn't move or remove its head; afterwards put moistened cotton inside an egg or garlic juice on the eye; after heat up the cautery which is divided: and over the head make like a formation of a quill pen, gather them as you are holding the cautery; if you see, should be pointed from one side to another, and if you see, it should also be like a tent; but in any case, whatever is held there serves your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula if it has opened, and treat the putrefaction, and dry it; and if it is closed, do work on it, and remove it from the body; afterwards place a form over the cautery, and hold your hand on the cautery at the part of the nose above the eye so that your hand doesn't make a mess; and place the cautery in the grease of the oil, and let it fester.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien. Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse .iij. jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se .xl. jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, that would be good. If not, restart the cautery one more time and again as needed, and leave it for three days; afterwards place moist cotton in butter, and apply the desiccating ointment until it's healed. If forty days have passed and it isn't healed yet, then apply a corrosive water medicine until the bone is exposed; and follow this prescription according to what comes in his chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent. Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure .i. camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	And there is a method for cautering fistulas that none of the old ones spoke about. Understand by fistula and open it; afterwards place inside the incision one thin camel's horn as you see fit:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	and I make it in quantity of three grains; and keep your hand or camel firm, so don't move the patient's body, making sure the melted wax doesn't run into their eye; then we should apply damp cotton in egg white or oil to the affected area: the wax will then heal the fistula and brings wonderful healing.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin. Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if the fistula is healed through the cautery as we have said, that's good. If not, then it is necessary to administer pertus to the child, and bring the fistula back inside the body near the nose according to what should be done in its own proper place.

de l’aposteme de la goule	from the abscess of the throat
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre. dou movement des dens	movement of the teeth

Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And by this manner the moving teeth are made stable again, and the softened gum is restrained, and the moisture that had caused corruption is dried.
de la dolor des dens	from toothache
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When toothache comes from coldness, or there is coldness or a fever, and medical treatments do not work, then it requires the use of cautery according to these two methods: and wax cautery and fire cautery.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Wax cautery if it's like this that you take cow butter and at the tip of a iron or snail spoon; after that take cotton and wrap it on the point of a needle, then soak the butter until it melts, and place it on the painful tooth quickly and hold it until it cools down; and do this often until its powers reach the root of the tooth, and if you see wet hair and cotton in cold butter, put them on the painful tooth again, and apply hot iron for as long as the fire reaches the tooth's pain.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain. Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	Fire cautery if it's like this that you take a piece of iron or snail, and make it big so that the fire doesn't reach to the edge of the wound; after heating the cautery, then the shape will come out afterwards, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the heat of the cautery cools down; do this often, because the pain will be relieved either that day or the next. And ensure that the patient fills their mouth with good butter during the process of applying the hot cautery, then quickly pull it out; and this is the form of the fire cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And make a fire cautery to whatever degree you desire, and according to what you are capable; and this is the form of the cure:
des scrophules	treat tuberculosis
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait ij. aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou .ij. se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi .iij. jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez. When the moisture invades the channels of the lung, especially when it comes from a cold constitution, then it is necessary to first empty the body with diuretic medicines. de ydropisie	Regarding cautery with fire, command the patient to allow the hair to grow long and even; and if they pierce at their base, hold the eyes still so they do not move until they grow.

Cautery is not suitable for dropsy, except by the method known as "asclytes". After leave the cauterization in place to heal for a long time, and do not stop the treatment of the illness after the cauterization; and recovery would hasten, and both methods (the cauterization and other treatments) would be combined with God's help.

And if you apply a large heated cautery, it will provide greater assistance.
de plaie mal curee	from a badly treated wound

When the patient's skin cannot tolerate cutting or opening, as we will explain in its section, if such a disease occurs that can only be cured through cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont. Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou .ij. ou .iij., selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes. se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	When there is no hole and it's aged with putrefaction and moisture corruption, if you test the entire area thoroughly, ensure that you know how many layers that hole has. And be cautious not to burn nerves or major veins. If the fistula goes into the body of the bladder or intestine, you need to take care with these areas, and do not perform this outside a surgical context, and remember that it isn't always an abscess; after treating the area until it is healed, when the pus has been drained long enough, then you know that the area is completely healed; and if the contents haven’t been drained out, know that the area is still infected, with corruption of bone at its base; in this way, as one of these we will speak about in our area.

de la hainche	From the thigh

de la dolor de la hainche	Regarding the pain in the thigh
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the thigh bone, and it is due to coldness and moisture, and patients are treated as we have said in the division, but the treatment does not work, and the disease is old: then you should cleanse the patient of the large humors using putrid pills or other beneficial similar pills.

And this is the method for sciatica, when pain stays in the hip, and doesn't reach up to the thigh nor to the leg. And if more work is needed, then do it; and if it appears that the pain lies between the knee and thigh, then perform cauterization with a surgical or circular instrument. Be well guarded in all your cauterizations making sure not to leave them incomplete until you burn nerves and large arteries, and do not cause the patient more harm and contraction than necessary.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez. Aprés une solution de ventre dont il ot la mort.	And I myself have seen many who performed cauterization on the ankle up to the knee, and left them so long that the leg swelled completely, and also all the toes, causing pain and corruption in all the toes. de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain of the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back, whether by falling or from percussion or due to an excess of evacuation, or due to any likeness of cold matter spread out, none of these likenesses warrant cauterization, because it is something that comes from the introduction of cold matter into the body.

de la routure dou syfac	Regarding the rupture of the uterus
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When division comes about in anger, and the veins descend into the intestines it is newly so, you should know that when you are curing him or her, do not eat meat for that day; and use things that lighten the stomach, so that the wind descends from his or her abdomen. tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles. de meselerie	Of cautery by fire, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they pierce at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.
