The cures are aided many times by cautery and also the illness that comes from the putrefaction of blood and melancholy. If you see a case to be treated with cautery, take care if the illness is at its beginning, and treat it according to what we have said in the division, without spreading or lingering, and doubt that corruption spreads throughout the body, then do this: five cauterizations on the head: one toward the back of the head starting from nine and the other towards the forehead at the end of hair; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the neck bone; and leave your hand so that the cautery reaches up to the bone, and until the scabs come out so that the vapors of the gross humors can escape; and cauterize on the cheeks according to what was mentioned above.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the moisture is everywhere dispersed; and it is clearly absent, then you should cauterize with these cauterizing tools that we have mentioned: one on top of the nose, and two cauterizations on the spine at the neck, and six cauterizations on the spine of the back, and one big one over the buttocks and another down below, and two on the shoulders; and two around the knees, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of hands and feet, and in the hollows of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are behind the last toe, do not burn them. And never cauterize over bone at the elbow, and one more on the bone of the stomach, and one more on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus. Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers. Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	And know that when I make more cautery burns, I give more aid, and it benefits him; and know that the patient does not feel pain from the cautery as a healthy person would, for their body is already completely corrupted. And it must be that the size of the cautery is large or small according to limbs and joints, just like you will find in descriptions of metal tools. After the treatment, powder it several times with honey and other cures until it is healed.
de enfleure	"De enfleure" translates to "of inflammation" in English. This term likely refers to a state of swelling or inflammation in medical contexts.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	When inflammation occurs in any limb and is treated with medicines and oils and bandages, and it remains unhealed, then one must make cauterizations on the limb according to the severity of the inflammation; and so that the cauterization penetrates somewhat into the flesh. Then treat with ointments until it heals. And at each time when a cauterization is done on the hand, foot, and back, at the point where the limb's nerve becomes dormant, and thus the inflammation is removed; and nonetheless, no one should interfere unless they are knowledgeable about limbs and the exits of moving nerves in the body.
de albaras	Of cautery from fire, command the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is advanced, and medicine in its original form proves ineffective, then apply a small amount of cautery using a fire cautery, according to the quantity of the root being burned, until the white part emerges and changes color; then treat with flour mixed with lentils several times along with rose oil and leaves of plantain, and blood from rooster and blood from duck, each in one part; mix all together, wrap it with a cloth, and let it be exposed on the affected area until it heals.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment for gangrene by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble .i. cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.  Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	When the boil begins and you see it stop, if you are to burn it off with a cautery, do so around the entire circumference of the boil. And always let them say that one should also burn in the center of the boil; yet I do not find this good for me either, as I fear that it might cause ulceration and corruption, and I have already decided against trying it any time; and a more logical method is to cauterize around it, with the round cautery named 'circule', as we described in the manner of using many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the boil that cannot die
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi. Car elle se hastera de meureir.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it doesn't seem to die either due to its excessive behavior or because of the old age of the illness when it's deteriorated (meaning it is too old), with little blood, or for some time; and you see that it needs to die faster: then burn off a bit of it with several small cautery treatments at a time; leave it like this. For it will hasten its death process.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it pierced right through with all the cautery, if you heat up this form of the cautery:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis. Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And place your hand in the middle of this disease which is called "adubelati" as long as the cauteries pierce the heart, and make them like these cauteries that the patient feels being pierced outwards in such a way that the progress of corruption is alleviated. After the cure until it is completely healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The cure by fire through iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches. Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit. Et puis le laisse .iij. jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption. Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.  Et se tu vois aprés .iij. jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus. Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	Another way of disease involves what is called "corrodens," and this refers to tissue damage in a limb. It damages the limbs just like fire burns dry wood. If you observe this disease affecting parts that can be treated with heat, then use cautery made of fire for that purpose. Make the cauteries in clavicles small and large as necessary depending on where the disease is present; after applying the cautery from all sides until you remove all corruption, leaving nothing behind so that no part of what has been corrupted remains. And then let it be for three days, apply burning with oil to the burnt areas while any scabs caused by heat are being removed and all corruption. After the treatment with ointments causing pus generation in chapter III. If after three days healthy tissue doesn't start growing, it's good; but if not, restart the cautery on what remains of the corrupted parts. This tissue damage can sometimes be cured with medicine instead of fire-cautery; however, fire-cautery is more effective help, and I have already discussed the treatment for ague medicine in section: take as needed when you have it available.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of stones that come to stones
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet. Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc .ij. manieres. C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude. Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe .i. cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi .iij. jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines. Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times, when stones pass through the body, an illness occurs that is called "clos" according to our understanding, and it's a large hardened lump that irritates the stone. The treatments for this kind of illness consist in two ways: fire cautery and hot water cautery. Fire cautery involves heating one cautery like a feather from a goose, made of good steel to match every size so it can be applied all around the stone, and it should have thin edges; after that, heat it up completely on top of the stone and quickly twist your hand around the stem until it reaches the bottom of the hole; then leave it like this for three days until pus starts to form; then make a poultice using ground wild marigold with oil, and let the poultice sit overnight. The hole will close up and the root of the lump will be removed. Then apply ointment treatment with purging charcoal until it heals.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines. Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	And if they are turned by the sides of the body, and this happens many times in hands and elbows, then it should be that you take a hot cautery; and do so as follows: take one from an arnica or iron, or a feather of woodpecker, place them on a nail and a thorn, which means for warts; then put the stick in such a way that it touches all parts completely. Next, apply a little hot water, hold your hand well, press your hand so that the edge of the stick reaches down to the root of the nail, and then find the hot water penetrates deeply right up to the root; let the patient endure the hot water burning for a short time, an hour or more; then leave them like this, and it will remove all its roots. Do this with each other until you have cleared off all these on your body, then treat any growths that produce pus.
li cure dou trembler	treatment for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	And when someone shakes due to cold or nerves, or malaria fever or other conditions, it should be that you do this: apply three or four hot applications on the spine of the back, one hot application between each vertebra; and one application under the fingers and one at stomach with the olive cautery. If this doesn't stop shaking, then hasten the recovery from the cold illness.
des pustules puans	pimple sores
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues. si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire. Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	No sign appears outwardly from the body of a person infected with pustules or putrefactive lesions that come from large decayed matter. When these signs first appear, one should apply cautery to each head of the pustule: a fine firebrand made from fir tree bark whose tip is taken up by the flame, or from long root of aristolochia, or with a lentil-shaped cautery. And when you cauterize them, not at the beginning but following this manner, they do not grow pus and spread further; instead, what causes the excess is dissipated, making them healthy. But it should be done after blood evacuation.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there have been great flows of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound, or during the incision of an abscess, or with the cautery on the limb, and similar situations; and it is very unpleasant to smell this.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to no one, if you hurry to place your index finger on the cut of the vein, hold it there until the pulse ceases under your finger and no more drop escapes; then heat several olive oil cautery tools, both small and large, until they are all red hot. Then take one, or a large one depending on the size of the wound and its location where the artery is routed, and place the cautery over that vein where you hold your finger, and keep the cautery in contact until the pulse has been extinguished.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it jumps out when you lift your finger from the vein, and the cauteries are extinguished, then take one of another cautery that is heated quickly.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And continue to apply this one after the other until the pulse has been extinguished completely; and beware that you do not burn the nerve underneath it, and that no harm comes upon the patient; know that when there is no beat of the artery, you cannot properly extinguish the pulse even if the artery is large, except through four methods as we have said: by cautery, or by extraction if it has not been treated, or by strong tightening of a thread, or by medicines placed on which have the power to extinguish the blood; and bind it and hold it in place.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever administers bandaging tightly with cloths or places burning objects upon them, or other similar things, if it does not benefit, they should not do so.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if such an event occurs and there is no sight or medicine available, should place their finger upon the wound of the vein as we have said, and properly extend it until the coldness remains above the wound and above the vein; and they must not move it but moisten it with cool water often enough until it becomes very cold so long that the finger is frozen, swollen and remains cold; and apply cauteries and medicines where necessary.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	This begins the second book on treatments for amputations
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases where it is necessary to use a fire cautery or medicine cauter, and their uses, causes, instruments, and forms of cauterization; and we placed that chapter up until the knee, and I will proceed with this chapter in the same manner for those who find them more easily understandable.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And as I begin this, it is necessary, dear child, that you understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than with the first uses of a cautery instrument, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often blood evacuation when opening veins, and incising abscesses, and treating wounds, and extracting arrows, and cutting into stones, among other things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie. Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures. si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	And I advise you not to engage in foolishness. For many ways of people come into cures. Some come from those who were so tormented by their illness that they died slightly due to the distress they found in their disease, and because of the severity of their suffering; and on these one must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse. Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	And of these I give their meaning and say: "Wait, I am the one with knowledge"; and disease is spiteful. It should not be that you agree to those who come to you in this manner, but rather place more respect for your honor than for your greed, and do not open foolishly but wisely about those you are certain of, and those you can understand; and use prediction and guidance in the treatments of your patients where health is converted; and this will help you to gain good reputation, fame, and lasting memory. And it will assist you in acquiring a prestigious name, glory, and remembrance for a long time.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Dear child, our kings give you good understanding and righteousness, and if you wish to inspire from the holy inspiration of their hand, so be it.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or if I have organized this chapter by devising it in parts according to chapters, specifically regarding the sections on cauteries as I devised them from the head down to the feet, so that you will find it easier to understand what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The head filled with water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Know that this disease comes about very often in infants at birth, and when the mother restrains the head of the infant too tightly; and it happens not because of any known reason.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never see this disease in anyone other than children, and among all those I have seen, death came quickly; and because of this, it seems to me that I should stop the work with these kinds of treatments.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw an infant of whom the shoulder was full of water, and the head swelled each day to such a degree that it could no longer bear it; and because of this moisture, he died. This moisture is assembled over the bone near the elbow, between the bone and the skin; and the surgical procedures are such that the moisture is between the bone and the skin, and the abscesses are small, causing you to cut into the head along a broad slit; and it goes as far as two inches in length while the moisture flows. And see here the shape of the suppuration:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If there is more moisture involved, and if the abscess is bigger, then make two incisions in a cross-like manner, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and if you see that the openings near the head on both sides are widened from each part, and the sharp pain increases when you press it with your hand inside, and this does not respond: then it is necessary to cut through the middle of the head with three incisions according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers. Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	And after the incision, remove all moisture. After restraining the cuts with bandages and powders, and I put wine and oil, and leave it like this until the fifth day; then release him, and treat the wound by turns and with applications, and let the head be restrained evenly, and once give meat to eat of dried flesh near moisture until the limb is strengthened and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the opening of the abscess is large, and the assembly of the water; for it is never in front; it is never behind; neither to the right; nor to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Then cut the place where the abscess opens and fill with water, make a cut according to what you are able to do; and be careful not to sever an artery; look for blood flow, so that the patient dies due to bleeding and removal of moisture.
de reume	regarding the treatment
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to anyone a disease called "catarrh" in the eyes or at the anus, and this illness is old, and the treatment with medicine does not help, then the last resort therapy would be the cauterization using which one severs those two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout .i. drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de .ij. pars. tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It therefore follows, if you observe them properly, that the patient should move their head; after this, rub the area with a coarse cloth until the arteries become visible, then pull out the hair's root by all means. Then look where the veins lie, and the ears of both sides are after the ears, and when they are restored. Then mark the ears with an 'X', then cut each one with an extremely sharp pair from half to three-quarters as much as the length reaches up to the bone, and this should be done by the width of their head's circumference.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you can see it, hold the blade near the artery and cut above it, also making a cut as deep as two inches through it.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein has been cut, make sure that the blood flows continuously outwards at the top.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de .iij. dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est .vj. c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins. selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery doesn't open upon feeling, you should measure the size of the space to be .3 inches. Then press and apply force until reaching the bone; and what needs to be done with the blood that needs to be removed is .75 ounces, plus or minus a little depending on how much the patient can bear and the filling of the artery. Then look at the wound: if it remains on the bone exactly like syphilis, if there's no sign of the pus at the abscess site, then press the incision tightly, apply bandages, and apply ointment until it heals.
de emigrainne	of headache
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old age headaches and acute colds arise, due to the moisture from tears and heat in the temples and forehead area as well as similar symptoms, it is treated through various methods of medical treatment and none of these help. Therefore, we should remove the veins of the temples and cauterize them, as we have recounted.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of their extraction is such that one should place themselves behind the hair on the temples of their patient and hear at the artery which opens in the temple, because it opens well through its beating and responds only within some very cold men; and if it does respond, then restrain their neck by some cloths of theirs, then rub their head with a rough cloth, and raise their head in hot water until the artery appears clearly. Then take the spatula from which this is made:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des .ij. chiés. Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	Then gently burn the skin until you hear from the artery, then pull it upwards with clamps, and remove well all the threads that are off each part; and if the artery is subtle, turn it at the tip of the hook, then hollow out that part according to the number of two heads. For if it is not hollowed out, it will not cut everything thoroughly everywhere.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And drain out six and seven times up to ten times; and if the artery is large, it is necessary that you tie it with two thick silk threads for double strength so that decay does not occur before the welding of the wound, and it does not recur with bleeding; then remove the excess matter between those two threads at that time itself, and then, if you see fit, gently cauterize up to the bone with a small cautery tool until the heads are hollowed out; this is the completed work, if the patient does not have fever and has hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cauterizations are aid to finish off the wetnesses: because it is more great aid for the wetnesses.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that we fill the entire area with old cotton and place good tents on top; and when they are released, if you apply dry medicine-making substances that produce pus, as well as tents, until they become clean; and if there's a lack of a copper piece in the artery, you must do it like what you perform, hurry by cauterizing or use the area filled with vitriol and hold it tightly with your hand so the wound becomes dry; and if you don't have that tool at hand, insert a small amount into the cotton until the wound is frozen, and rinse the cotton in cold water until pus stops coming out, then hold it properly. And the one who is slower and lighter during the extraction of the artery should cauterize the skin of this cauterization trenching for two parts, but make sure the trenchings are well separated to last longer with heat.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the tools are too tight, it retains less of its heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be between the two knives an inch of space, and then when you mark to close the two ends, and you place the hot iron up until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in both places; and they must be separated by about one inch because this cautery does not stick throughout completely; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are draining through veins above the neck bone at the head's back, and no benefit is received from the medicine being applied there, you'll see the skin turn red in response to it, and feel your forehead pulsate as if with a fever; and wherever they are damp and moist so that paper hairs fall off, and the papers heat up due to this, and are burned by the heat of the tears, then this treatment must be used.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai .iij. fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com .ij. doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres .ij. as .ij. costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as .ij. costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des .ij. mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de .iij. dois au traver joins;	And they named the old 'treatment for burns', and you should instruct the patient suffering from this illness to have hairs on their head or forehead, then make him three cuts evenly across the forehead according to its length; let one of these cuts be as long as two doves laid end-to-end on the front, and the others two cuts are each above ribs, and avoid cutting into arteries that lie above ribs; keep your hand away from connecting points of the two jawbones, and ensure each wound area is about three doves in length across.
et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de .ij. pars de coi ci est li forme:	And have an absorbent sponge and some cloths ready to wipe away the blood, then use a hot broth from two parts of what follows this form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	After making the cut behind the temple up to the second cut; and burn all the skin that is between the two cuts completely until it reaches the flesh above the bone. Then cut further along the middle cut up to the other end, and then remove this hot broth.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	If there's a first cut in the opening made with the tool known as "cutter", and it is very sharp on one side, while on the other side it's blunt, not sharp, and this has the form:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure. Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the cutting edge towards the inner flesh at the elbow, and the blunt edge towards the bone, and make the cut until it reaches half-way through. And remove all vessels that descend from the head to the bones as long as the incision continues up to where it opens at the elbow, and then do this further halfway in the first incision up to the other opening; and then remove the blood evenly, expressing the limb for the blood taken; then place a piece of old cotton in each incision, and apply wrappings soaked in vinegar and oil and garlic, and ensure no pus leaks out; and on the third day release the bandage, and provide a large amount of water bathing, then apply the ointment cure with rose oil, and other cures for wound healing, until they heal completely.
dou reume des eulz	from the pus
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When it comes to sudden catarrh (illness) accustomed to occur, and you see the eyes red and small, and weakening of vision, and burnt paper; and the hair is greasy, and one sweats profusely in fever, and the body shivers; then know by these occurrences that those substances and that catarrh do not come from many veins, and the moist cure that it is, if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large. i. poc. Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les .ij. levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And you instruct the patient to look behind their forehead, then make a large cut through the forehead, and another broad. Start from the temple on the left side to the temple on the right side, and with this incision go up to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move during eating; and when the bone is revealed, bleed it all out using a sponge, then cleanse between the two lips of the incision and place old cotton wool, and linen fabric; then cover with wet cloths in wine and oil, and avoid removing any pus; once the bone has been removed, you should rub the bone until flesh begins to grow, then treat with desiccating substances that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this manner: take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of coloflorence, and make a paste; and apply this paste to the wounds to promote flesh growth everywhere.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the burning of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that is inserted into the ears is one of the four things: or grains, or beast, or mine stones or similar things such as iron; or seed, such as beans, peas; or flowing matter such as water and air and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel. Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus. Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	When he inserts into the ear a stone or any other thing that does not fit in the ear or does not grow in the ear, then place the ear under the sun. If you see the stone, if there is no drop of violet oil or nut oil distills, then proceed with extraction; and make him sneeze with camphorated oil, and stuff the nostrils when the sneezing comes, and put pieces of cloth or wool into the ear; and keep the ear above. Many times this cure succeeds; and if it does not succeed, then proceed with extraction using fine forceps, as follows:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps out with the forceps, that's good; if not, proceed with extraction using fine forceps of small double curvature; and if it does not jump out through this, then make a spider's thread and plug the end of the thread or the ear wick strongly, and stuff wax into the part inside the thread so that nothing can enter the hole with the thread; then pull forcefully, because many times it succeeds as we have said; and if it doesn't succeed in this manner, then take some glue from this, mix it with its oils, put a small tool suitable for this task, and place a little cotton inside; then press the glue onto the stone or whatever it may be, and pull forcefully.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if she does not respond to all these things that we have mentioned, you must quickly make an incision into the ear in order to drain pus and abscesses, and relieve the pain. The method of this cut is that you first displace the head of the ear with the help of the patient's cephalic bone, and remove blood according to its natural extent, then place the head back between your hands and turn the ear upwards, making a small incision at the base of the ear near the fatty part hanging down; and make the cut in such a way that it resembles a crescent moon as you approach the bone. Then break through the bone according to your capability and suck out quickly into your mouth; and continue this until it's clean.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grains that are inside and they swell up, you should administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then administer a thin spatula according to this shape:
et amenistre incision de celui grain. Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	And make an incision to that grain. But do not perform this if you think the grains are moist due to the moisture of the ear, until you have made many pieces; then remove them with fine forceps and suction, just like we said, so that the extractions become easy.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton. Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est. s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin. se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent .i. jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	In the cold indeed when one sneezes in the ear then it's appropriate for patients to use their nostrils to expel the first discharge and expand the ear with old cotton. And lie flat on that same or ear where the cold is. If it jumps out through this, well done. If not, take several stones according to their lengths and gently, and heat them a bit at the fire; then place one or two of them inside his or her ear, and stand from one foot on the other side, and make an incision with another stone on the stone that is in the ear; and keep performing this from stone to stone until all the cold comes out entirely, and thus it jumps out completely. And if you see, take one stick, and place one of the heads inside the ear, and the other head in fire until the more sensitive stick burns; then redo another set of sticks until all the cold comes out, as we have explained with stones.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the beast, if it is of small size, like a flea and similar things, treat it as we have said in division; but if it is of large size that one can feel, perform the extraction with forceps; and this is the more gentle thing to remove which is inside the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of the worms in the ears, when you follow the treatments as we have said in division and regarding distillations, and if the cure does not help, then it is necessary that you observe the ear under the sun: if there are no worms visible, then remove them with fine forceps; and if nothing can be seen, then take this form of cane which is described here.
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus. Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent. Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And let it be narrow at the bottom and wide at the top. And use the thinnest part of the tool according to the extent of the patient's suffering, then apply force throughout the entire canal; do this repeatedly until all the pus has come out. And if they do not want to come out, immerse the cotton inside the canal as I have described in relation to cutting worms; and if they do not protrude like we said, administer distillations that the old ones have tested in worm incisions, and you will find guidance on distillation treatments; and distil your oils and medicines into the ear through this instrument, which is shaped as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And let it be made of silver or lead, with a narrow end at the bottom and .i. small tube above for distillation; and to press within the distillation use .i. properly made tool from lead suitable for this purpose, and if you see .i. rasp attached to the tip wrapped around the inner extension in cotton; then pour your oil or juice, and what you see of your medicines inside the tube, and the tube is in the ear; then push within the rasp all the cotton, and press your hand properly until the oil is distilled or out of the ear; and feel the patient internally, and let one hot distillation be poured for .i. minute with fire as it's done in the ear; and keep it from being too cold, because the medicine wouldn't be so good.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Regarding ear piercing.
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without any hair on their ears; and this same thing happens to adults due to wound impalement or a fetus forming inside the ear, and these wounds never enter the ear, so one cannot see them; and neither does it happen that two hairs emerge from the absence of hair, and one can see this clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes in through the wound, if one cannot see it, is of concern for its internal healing at various stages, and you should understand that when it's appropriate to place the ear under the sun; and look inside: if you see the obvious growth, if the work has completed this form of pus that I've mentioned.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And let it be so when cutting in front and behind completely flat surfaces, ensuring no harm to the ear; if there's a growth due to pus or part of the ear, use fine needles to pinch it gently until all that is purulent has been removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren .i. raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille. de la porriture de l’oil	Regarding the decay of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de .ij. manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.  Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	When this disease, called 'aleacrati' or 'putrefaction', comes about in the eye, there are two ways: one natural, and the other unnatural. And it occurs suddenly from a wound, or from cutting, or from burning, and through similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent. And the way of the operation in this is that you cut open that seam, and uncovers the eyelid, and puts linen cloths inside it, and binds it until it heals; and it is not advisable to use things in its treatment that dry and restrain. Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasures of your cure are that you must beware not to reattach it in a form as it was before; and the operations we have spoken about do not go beyond treatments for this disease so that it does not return in the same form as it was before.

de l’ungle de l’oil	of the eye's eyelid

de la bowe de l’oil	From the bowl of the eye
