de la char sor le neis	from the flesh at the nose
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color. En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; puis cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	None of them are born or raised as knotted flesh balls of various kinds; some resemble scorpions in appearance. If there is a ball with a reddish color and if it has a good flesh color, then for such cases where the ball isn't red, you should have the patient lie under the sun between your hands. Squeeze their nostrils and pour vinegar on these balls, then remove them. Next, apply what can be held by hand to the very fine sharp point of the spatulum tool on one side until you know that the ball is fully extracted.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if there remains no matter we cannot remove, if you open up to allow the use of all one instrument finely lightly, ensuring nothing stays; and should it not ascend, or pus appear, then seek it out as seems fit; and should these be malicious pus, act swiftly and apply heat until the pus is stopped and every hair is removed completely, then pour water or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, acoi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes .i. fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice .i. doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil. Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu .iij. jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	And if it remains open and wetters come up to the throat, know that there is pus present; and should no wetter pass as it should, know that there's flesh formed inside the bone above, where the instrument doesn't go for cutting: thus, you need to take a thread of linen somewhat thick, and fasten it between your thumbs, ensuring an inch or less spacing between each knot; and put the patient down on their side with the thread in their nose by force, pulling it out with fragrance until it comes through the nostril within the mouth; and many times this is done to children at school, as it's a simple task for those who wish to do so; then hold the head coming out of the nostril with one hand, and the other head coming out of the mouth with the other hand, making sure you know which comes next as we guide them with our fingers. Do this until you're certain that each knot has rotted away any flesh, then pull the threads, clean off any blood, moisten the thread in Egyptian ointment and put it back at the nose exactly as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments have corroded all that remains of flesh; and afterwards place a clove in the nostril for a few days until it's healed, and if you need dried medicines, use them; and this is how the tool purges the head, to which oil and medicines are distilled or used with vinegar:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or arsenic, resembling an open lamp, like a rod, and guide him thus; and if you see fit, make a closed rod, and have your instrument filled for purging the head; and hold one end of the rod when you heat oil or any liquid.
de la char sor le neis	from the nostril's wax
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times at the root of the nose a disease is born which is called 'telul', it grows and becomes large to see; and because this requires that you catch it at its beginning, then remove all bone, afterwards place in the middle the cautery or hot medicine; and if one delays catching it until it's big, they must beware if it's hard, changes color, loses sensation: don't touch it with iron as it is an infected abscess, for when you catch it once, it causes great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is due to heat contact, not due to losing color, and you see that one can catch all of it, then empty the patient and treat the area with dry and restraining substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the nose has been treated and sewn up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes. Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les .ij. levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Know that when solutions of continuance arrive in one of these bodily veins, they benefit little or not at all in many individuals. Therefore, it's necessary that this event doesn't occur to anyone, if you observe the wound is still bleeding from its entire blood; and then adjust the two edges to a seam, proceed with treatment until it heals; and should the edges are already dried on both sides, it's essential to sear all parts of their area until they heal, then join the two edges to a seam, and hold them together, powdering with dragon's blood powder and incense ground. And place the powders on a plaster piece of strong or another solderable plaster, and leave it until it discharges by itself, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of the seam is such that you join the material: or with threads, as we have said in the abdominal seam; or with string, as I have informed you.
des apostemes des levres	removal of abscesses from lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	With the cautery of fire commanding the unwell to let hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
de la char des gencives	From the pulp of the gums
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times, bone pieces arise on the gums that are attached, which the ancients called "albulus"; you should hold it with forceps and remove it to its root, allowing for bleeding or blood; then place it under vitriol powder, or other drying and restrictive powders; if this flesh returns after incision and many times occur, when you remove it again, cauterize it: if it doesn't return even after the cautery; these are the forms of instruments to remove it.
des sordens	Of cautering with fire, instruct the patient to allow the hairs to grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold them steady so they do not move until they grow.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Some occasions are gathered at the root of the teeth within the mouth between the gums, and unpleasant and rough layers; and several times there is a black tooth with citrine stones and worms until the decay reaches the gum, and the teeth become stinking. Therefore, you need to hold the patient in your hands and have their head on the floor, and pull out the teeth or the scales that you see, as long as nothing remains; and then perform on the darkness and greenness, and yellowness and other tones until they are removed. And if what needs to be taken out is done at the first occasion, it's good; if not, start again the next day and the third day, until you have everything pulled out. Know that teeth require various types of instruments for pulling, according to what the work shows, because the scraper that pulls teeth from outside has different shapes than that which is pulled between the teeth; these shapes and others should be ready with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth for its pain that you delay removing it as long as possible, because one should not do this; because this is a very high material up to there therefore there should be no excuse for pulling.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant. Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	So when the patient is forced to extract the tooth, you must be sure of which tooth hurts. Often during pain, one believes it is a holy tooth, and attempts extraction of the good tooth; but until the bad tooth is fully removed, do not depart from this pain, as we have already taught our healers; and when you are certain about the hurting tooth, it is necessary to cauterize around the tooth with one or two spatula-sized burns to protect the gum from all sides; then move your hands or use your fine forceps gently, bit by bit until it is fully extracted, then secure well the forceps; and have the shoulder of the patient in your holy hands between your knees, and keep him still so he does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier. Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	After extracting the tooth properly without breaking it off, and if it doesn't fall out on its own, take none of these instruments and gently push them inside from each side, and shake him as you did initially. And if there is a hole where the tooth was lost, then it's necessary to fill it with gauze at the site that got loose; and if it needs to be extracted precisely using forceps, see that it doesn't break while being pulled; and it must be sharply opened around the gum to remove the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere. Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And see to it that you do not break him and leave a piece inside. Inform the patient about this by telling them that they will experience greater pain from the root due to malice later on after the initial extraction. And remember that don't act like ignorant healers who, out of haste and recklessness, break everything once and don't follow our teachings. Instead, allow complications to come in only one instance through the operation of this great disease because of the roots that remain or the bones they break, as we often desire; and when the tooth is extracted, wash his mouth with wine or water and vinegar; and if bleeding occurs (which it often does), then fill his mouth with vinegar; and if this doesn't work, cauterize him.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the tools, with which you make your teeth first, should be long-pointed and have large handles, so they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And may have large parts that do not bend during use, and they should be made of well-crafted iron, with teeth for holding them securely.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre .i. jor ou ij., tant que li leus soit amolis, puis i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	When the root remains during extraction, it is necessary to put moistened cotton inside the mouth with butter for one or two days until the gums are softened. Then remove the forceps called "algefri," making the shoulder seem like a well-tended beak; and they should be made in this manner:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to emerge from all these tongs, then you must uncover the flesh completely along the root and place an instrument which is called "althali", meaning palainche, as it appears in this form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And make it hollow and thick so that it doesn't break at all, and if the root jumps out through this, it's good; if not, use all of the instruments, as their forms come after this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you have to help with this tool that has two points, as it appears in this form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other tools that are arranged in the proportion of teeth in front, and with this tool that seems like large pincers, as it appears in this form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And be aware of this tool so it cannot break, and know that many tools of bone exist; similarly with other tools which are not named; and also skilled surgeons find their own instrument on their own according to what their tasks and diseases show them. For there are parts of diseases where the old did not teach any tools due to their variety; and if it breaks from carrying or another bone, or if it rots when it should remain solid, if they seek out the tool they need among those I've mentioned, and help through gestures, as shown here is its formation:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And may they be large and well holding to hold the bone, so it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then return him to his place with medicines that suit this. And if there is decay in the bone and it is small, if he uses all of this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form, and it is ugly in shape, especially in maiden women, if you need to know whether the teeth have been born after the tooth and are not in their proper place, and cannot be worn or filed: then extract it; and if there is connection with the tooth, take this instrument as described here which resembles a pair of small hooks, and made of sharp iron.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the bite is made little by little in my hands because of the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move others, and if it appears that one could shave it off, then I grind it with a piece of stone as shown here:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it's also like the file used to make needles; and I grind the tooth slowly by hand lightly, so that it doesn't move until it finishes; then you level off at the end with a rasping tool, and if it's too sharp causing pain in the tongue, then you need to smooth out its roughness until it becomes even, so that it does not cause pain in the tongue nor damage speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is heated
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les .ij. dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a .i. ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper. Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des .ij. dens sains, et des .ij. meus, si com tu vois:	When the tooth is impacted within the mouth, through percussion or impaction, and when the patient cannot press upon it to cause evacuation of pus, and you have treated it with restricting medicines, this method isn't effective; then you should restrict it with a golden thread, for silver threads turn green and decay, but gold does not change ever. And take a thread that's neither too thin nor too thick, according to the size of the gap between the teeth; and if you notice a fitment of teeth, take the thread and hold both ends together between two healthy teeth, then place the dislocated tooth between the diseased teeth, whether there is one or more, until you see it properly on the other side of the healthy tooth; then continue with covering until reaching your starting point, and pull your hand subtly and precisely, until it no longer moves; and bind your thread to the root of the tooth so that it can't escape. Then cut the threads near the tooth with pincers, gather them together, place them between a healthy tooth, and set it in such a way that it doesn't injure the tongue; and then leave it compressed as long as it can stay, if it comes loose or if the threads break, you will have to tighten it with another thread; if it stays and serves like this throughout its time, this is the natural position of teeth and the fitment between two healthy teeth, and two diseased teeth, just how you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is removed, if it's placed back in its socket gradually, as we've said; and don't intervene with anything other than what you're instructed to do and can bear, and at no point make a form like an ox bone tooth, and place it in the socket where the defect is, then tighten it as we have described, and it stays and serves for as long as possible.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	covering the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder. Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	No time is spent on the ties which come from the tongue or nature that we are born with; or by accident due to a healed wound; and these operations consist of working in your mouth towards the illness, having your head healthy, lift the tongue; then cut off the nervous ligament across its width, until the tongue has been lifted out of its position. If there is hardness or clotting, it’s due to sudden wounds, so pinch off the hook and cut across that connection; and ensure that the cut isn’t too deep as it’s near blood vessels; once done, lift your head from a pinkish watery state and ease away, then put over the tongue a linen cover; and rub the illness every night, making sure the tongue doesn't heal. And if bleeding occurs, place vinegar on your head instead; and if the wound doesn’t heal, cauterize using the slow-burning cautery, which is good for this purpose; then continue to treat with other cures until it has healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it to be of any color or blackness or hardness that the illness doesn't feel, do not touch it for it's a sore; and if it declines towards yellow fever, and there is moisture present, use the hook on it and cut with a fine incision from both sides, then release it on all sides; and if your wound doesn’t heal in your operation, place vinegar on it until it stops bleeding, then return to your operation as long as you apply force; then lift your head away from wetness and ease, and continue other treatments until it has healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	extraction of throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les .ij. amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer. Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez. Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	No time passes within the throat glands that are called "godath," and they should properly be called the two almonds. And when you treat them, as we have said in division, if they aren't healed, take care: If it's pus-filled abscesses with a small sense of touch and fusse color, don't touch them with metal at all. And if they are red and the root is large, don't touch them with metal either, for fear of blood spilling; but leave them until they're sore, then you will remove them, or it would burst on its own; and if it's white in color retains, and the root is subtle, have your instrument ready to scoop, but first ensure that the pus-filled areas are calm and pacified. Then let the patient stand under the sun, with their head in a good position of health, and have them open their mouth while you grasp their servants' hands between theirs, and press the tongue down over all the tool, as shown here; and may be made of silver or finely crafted gold just like knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue with all this tool, and see the pus-filled abscess? Take an onion and place it in the almond, and pull it up harder than you can; take nothing from the tissues with it, then scoop it out with your tool, as shown here; which looks like some strength. Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this tool at hand, scoop it out with forceps, as shown here:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make the incisions on one side and the other; and when you have completed one of the almonds, complete the other in the same manner, and after the incision gargle the sick with hot water, or hot and easy-to-swallow water, and if blood drainage occurs, gargle with hot water, or peelings of cooked cherry stones, or leaves of myrtle, and similar things, until the saliva is completely drained; then complete the cure until it becomes well; and do not allow any new abscesses to form in the throat other than the two almonds, then proceed similarly as for the two almonds.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir .i. aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi .i. jor ou .ij. Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis .ij. rains par les .ij. pertuis dou neis. Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un .i. oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	And I treated a woman of an abscess that was inside her throat, to be precise, a small abscess. I had almost completely sealed the entire throat passage, so much so that the woman couldn't breathe due to the obstruction, and could neither eat nor drink, she died if she stayed like this for one day or two days. The abscess had risen so high that it had placed two ropes through both nostrils at birth. I acted quickly then, put an inch of wax into one nostril first, then pulled it out with a large portion of grease; then made another cut under the other nostril, and got her to open her mouth while pressing her tongue. After inserting the wax in these abscesses, I took out some of them, only a little bit of blood came out. And thus opened up the passage for breathing inside the woman's throat, she could now drink water and then wine, without stopping my continuous cutting through that abscess; and the abscess would grow back again and fill the space I had emptied, to such an extent that it grew quite large; then I took care of her and cauterized inside the throat: thus did not continue growing; and I left these parts, may only God do good after me.
de l’uve	from the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve». Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li. Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide. Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a .i. des .ij. estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres. Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des .ij. amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee. Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor. Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague. Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	When the bile rises in the eye, and it swells up and is long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is large and round, it's called "bile". When it is treated as we have said in division, and the treatment doesn't help, and you see that the pus has subsided, and it is subtle; then you must remove it. And when this one is round and assembled and isn't long; and if it's bloody or of a mustard color or black, then you should avoid making an incision in this case. For there is great danger to the patient. Therefore, whenever you see it according to how I've said with regards to its smell and lengthiness, have the patient face the sun, press their tongue onto the tool as we made remembrance of previously; after that, insert the pin into the bile, then drag it outwards, and remove it using two tools we described in incision of two almonds. And you should not use too much force when removing, only up to what is beyond its natural end; because if you take more than necessary, it may hurt the voice or speech afterwards. After the incision, use what we said about incisions of almond, and treat until the patient recovers. And if your patient faints due to this removal, then when using cautery on this case, use something that makes them feel less pain. The manner of the cautery is sharp. Then let the patient's head get into your healthy state again, and after pressing their tongue onto the tool we described in chapter about cautery, press it with a lively blade until it isn't too thick or too thin; then utilize the movement of this tool, as described here:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place our head with a hair or where we put the medicine, like in the movements of a spoon, and place the tool across all the medicine on the bile; and let the patient remain stationary on their side, so that saliva and mucus flow from their mouth towards the medicine inside, ensuring it doesn't descend into the throat, and the wound heals. Then keep your hand over the medicine and press it onto the bile for half an hour's worth of quantity until you see that the irritation and actions of the medicine are subsiding; and if you notice this, take cotton and wrap it around any tool, moisten the cotton in the medicine, and place the tool on all the cotton above wax, until the cotton dries on the bile. And repeat this process as needed until the cauterization is perfect, then leave it to dry, and wait for four or five days afterwards. If you need to restart with medicine cauterization, do so, and after the cauterization of inside the bile, clean up that which was inside the medicine using a buttered cloth; rinse with cold water, and continue gargling until fully recovered.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This remedy is safer than the incision, not just the cautery; if it is treated with fumigation using this method, take camomile and myrrh and wormwood and rue and mint and similar herbs, and gather them all or any of them into one pot, and pour water into it, and let it boil; and ensure the pot is well sealed with strong earth, and in the middle of the pot place one cooking utensil according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut. Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And make it of silver or tin, and have one of the shoulder blades placed in the mouth against the sore until the vapor rises up the nose into the eye, until the eye is dead; after that repeat often, until the eye dries out, and be sure not to do this at the beginning of pus ejection, for many things occur; and don't do this when it's nearing the end of pus ejection. And if this instrument isn't available, take a stick and place inside your mouth an eggshell, so that there is no unnecessary heat in the mouth; because the eggshell doesn't let the vapor weigh down the mouth, and it's a good combination to heal together for safety.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times, open in the throat bone or spine of fish, without anything else; if it is thus that you should apply what you can see, press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you may observe movement; and that which does not open at all and remains in the throat, you should make the patient vomit until the substance leaves; by chance if this thing is expelled through vomiting; or if the substance swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a small piece of dry bread; and attach to the sponge a thread, then swallow it again; and when she comes up to the surface, if it rises, and then proceed to draw out. And if this thing does not come out from what we have said, take one of a cork instrument according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.
