de la sansue de la gorge	of the windpipe
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit. Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout .i. petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu. Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine .i. fer chaut, et fai ce sovent. Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor. puis pren plein .i. voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	No treatment is given for the windpipe, as I have mentioned in division, through medicine therapy; and when this does not help, then look inside the throat of the patient towards the sun, press their tongue with the tool I've instructed you on. And if you see the windpipe, guide it slightly, to a length of half an uncia (an ancient unit), or use fine tweezers suitable for this task. If this doesn't work, take a hair and insert it into the throat towards the patient's discomfort; then pull out one or two hairs until a noticeable change occurs, repeating this often. If the patient feels cold water, fill up to half a pint with cold water, wash their mouth with it, and swallow while moving your hand frequently; and as soon as the windpipe feels the water, they will vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier. Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes .i. pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And if it doesn't heal as we have said, then fumigate the patient with asafetida, using the tool we've mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this many times because it will heal without causing damage. And this is how to perform the fumigation: take one pot containing burning charcoal sticks and cover its middle part with a perforated lid; then place the end of the tool inside the lid's hole. After that, pour your fumigation into it, and put the tip of the stick in the patient's mouth, seal their mouth so that no fumes escape but only reach deep into their sinuses; now this mucus will come out, and if it doesn't heal, restart the fumigation multiple times. Allow the patient to be thirsty, eat salty things and similar, do not drink water; then eventually she needs to leave by this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	The form of the tool that treats the mucus, when you can see it, resembles curved tongs for moving things into the throat; and at the tip, it has a shape like a doctor's beak, and it also has a rasping edge, so whatever she takes cannot leave; now see this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en .ij. manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor. Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors. car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	No mention of discharges are there, according to what memory brings forward from one and another in this book, they vary in perforation and size; and it's done in two ways whereby one is in its own form, and because of the moisture it holds. And the second way is for bones within the body. For abscesses on the head are different than those on the base, and abscesses on the fatty part of the body are different from those that come at joints, and each has their judgment in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures. Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre. Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	And if there are abscesses one should not pierce them until the body is dead according to its completion; and for such as it is necessary to pierce when they have grown but do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that come from joints. For when abscesses come from joints, and you leave them while still within, by chance if both the tendon and nerve of the joint are corrupted because this causes contraction in that member. Or if the abscess is within the main limb, and if you delay perforation until it is dead, it will harm the principal limb; or if it's within the base, piercing should be done while it's dead; and one should not pierce an immature abscess without completed digestion except for those that are within the base which could grow fully through and remain inside, leading to a fistula; and would not heal in a large manner.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it should be known when the time is for perforating the abscess which has died according to its completion, and this is when the pain eases, and the departure of fever, and the reduction of pain and redness, and from the movement and sharpness at the head of the abscess, and other signs; and it should be done where the perforation stays higher above the abscess or below it depending on its location, and where it opens outwards; and make the perforation long through the body, and if the abscess is in hands or feet, joints and nerves and arteries, and all places where there are no wrinkles.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre. Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit. Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui. Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.  Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com .i. drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en .iij. angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	Among those who bend, according to that member. And when abscesses are in the fatty parts of the body, if they burst you should allow the perforation until it is confirmed by digestion being completed, as we said before. For if you pierce ahead of this, they will stretch along his body with the venom from him and become filled with a lot of dirt; and by chance make his skin hard and the depth of him. And for any abscesses that are pierced across the width of the body, according to what the limb needs. And it should be that you remove small abscesses, small pus-filled sacs; and in large abscesses, large pus-filled sacs, and many cuts according to the size of the abscess; and for those abscesses where it is necessary to have a knife's cut, and cover; when it has become as big as two pieces of cloth, and is flattened, then it should be done in this way for milk blisters: and for those that are split into three angles, and those that need to be covered like the leaf of myrtle, like abscesses from the angles; and for those where a round cut is made, and other cuts and similar cutting methods.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites. Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois. Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those who do not have a head, such as superficial abscesses, you should pierce them fully; and when the abscess is large, and has built up much pus, if you pierce it, do not drain all of the pus at once in that moment, but only a part of it. Then stop the incision until another day, then leave nothing to interfere; repeat this method gradually larger to larger, until the pus comes out completely; similarly when the patient's strength is weak, or pregnant women, or young children, or elderly people who are decrepit. Because the abscesses shudder many times with the exit of the pus, and by chance kills the patient, and you do not notice it. Therefore be cautious in this chapter, and if you have pierced your abscess, when it heals, check if the wound from the abscess is small; and if it's a full cut, provide linens or old cotton to dress it; and for large abscesses, with much pus, each of them should have tents that lie one against another. And if you have made a part in the skin in the abscess and covered it internally, then fill it with old cotton or linen wadding without moisture, and tie it until the third day; then wash, and treat with ointment until it heals properly.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille .i. drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.  Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blood flow occurs in your body part, dress with cold water and ease it, and moisten with a piece of cloth, and place it on the wound several times. And if the blood flow persists, take care of it and treat it, and use the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and if it's due to fever or if your body or abscess is very nervous, then you should apply moist tents and cloths soaked in wine and oil; and if it is in a state of fatness and your body is fatty, then it would be appropriate to place pieces of cloth soaked in water and oil, or in wine and cold oil until the third day, as we have said; and then remove the wound dressing and clean and treat it properly until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in treatments of abscesses: I have told you how one should proceed before treating abscesses, and here comes the chapter.
des soros	of the womb
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances. Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire. Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout .i. estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient. Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc. Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit. Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li apostemes tient .i. nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés. Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	Where small abscesses come from, and their methods are as if they're in cloths, like the tail of a cat, and many resemble these. There are some that are fat and some with moisture just like mice; and there are others that are hard and stony to the tailor, and there is no doubt that the artery doesn't oppose this. And the work of the operation comes from that you prove through all .i. tool which is called "entromissoire", its shape comes after this, what it contains. For if it contains moisture, then let it cut through long. And when the moisture is drained, then remove without leaving anything inside the skin containing that moisture, because it returns immediately once you leave nothing; then dip cotton in Egyptian ointment if available; if not, in water and vinegar, and apply to the wound and leave until the other day; and this follows what stays for the night. And after renew the cotton as before on the second day, and the third, until you know that it doesn't stay overnight; then treat the wound with ointment according to your convenience, until it heals. And if the abscess remains .i. hard, then cut along this shape, long; and let all your treatment dry inside the garment where it is; and if the artery opposes this, then do what I told you afterwards. And similarly treat when it's stony, and to the tailor and to treat as I said.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc. Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut .i. apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere. En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	And concerning the treatment of abscesses containing stones and moisture, it is more effortless, because there is little blood involved. And if any of these abscesses or boils are without moisture, and among those were two abscesses that I dealt with around an elderly woman; and found the abscess to be like a hard stone, rough and white, and unable to break; and even if one had not pierced through them, they would have been treated just as well for stones. In other types of abscesses, it was observed that those coming from around children's heads and ear roots, the opening needs to be left open for as long as possible to allow pus to drain; and treat them accordingly.
des scrophules	regarding scrophula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre. Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes. Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit. en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les .ij. levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	Many times abscesses occur in the neck, and when they rupture, and in anger, and nowhere else or on the body, and are small, and stick together. And each scrophula is properly contained within its case, just like a nut and an abscess around the head, as we have mentioned; and there are many appearances of these scrophulas. Some contain moisture, and others are malign and do not wish to obey treatment. In such cases that you observe good disposition towards the doctor, and resemble the color of the neck, it remains silent from each part and is neither close to the ears nor near the artery or in the conduit, and is not deep; then it's right that you cut over them, and peel off each part, and use two knives for the corners if necessary, as we have said about abscesses around the head; and treat it little by little, make sure not to cut into the nerve or the vein, and avoid excessive cutting that your hands slip away, don't go too far ahead when you are not supposed to cut.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir. Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde. Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it doesn't allow you to open, then put in the wound vitriol broil, or any powders that expel blood, and restrain the wound; and leave it as long as the abscesses are soothed, and the wound has softened, and begins to decay. And when the blood has been expelled, return to your work until you have completed it; then stop according to your duty index if there remain no small scabs, then remove them. And if there is a large vein in the root of the scab, it should not be that you cut that scab at its root but bind it with a double thick thread and let it fall through it without harm; then apply the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then start treatment.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les .ij. levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule. si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit. Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cut the entire scab, it should be that you join together the two sides of the wound and stitch them now, then there is no remaining of excess due to the size of the scab. It should be that you attend to cutting the root of it, drain it out, and stitch as we have said. Those scabs containing excess, pierce where it opens up; and pierce in this manner like those previously mentioned, by hanging, then apply healing things with ointment and similar items, so they decay what is remaining of corruption; and when the wound has been thoroughly cleaned, treat with an ointment covering flesh until it is clean.
de squinance	Regarding obliquity or deviation
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke and wrote about the surgery of cutting the throat; but I never saw anyone do this in our land, it's just recorded from their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those who have squinting eyes, it is necessary that the incision of the throat known as "epiglottis" be performed; and one should not attempt this procedure alone, because all the veins and the windpipe are in danger for those with pus-filled abscesses either in their mouth or in the throat or between the two mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is within the lymph channel of the windpipe, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the loss that comes from suffocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz .iij. cercles ou .iiij. une petite fendure dou travers, entre les .ij. cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige;	So, when we wish to cut the epiglottis, it is necessary that we make three or four small cuts through it, between the two circles, so that the size of the cut does not touch the cartilage.
et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	And these lungs can be subjected to the division of the epiglottis where there is no fat, and the vessel is long outwards.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit;	And if the surgeons are fearful, it is necessary for them to extend the skin of the neck up to the whole oncine, then cut through the bone until they reach the cartilage; and avoid blood vessels, if you see any substance, and then close the site as we have said.
et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix;	and it is demonstrated by the section of the stream from the cartilage which jumps forth through the limb that has been broken, and due to the loss of voice.
et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed during which one doubts strangulation, bring together the two sides of the wound neatly, and all along the seam without touching the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause healing flesh to form, until it becomes sound.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albanus states that one should not perform this until the entire throat is blocked, and the patient is deemed dead, and there is absence of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort;	Then one must cut the epiglottis because the patient cannot breathe normally. They will breathe through the wound and thus be kept alive from death.
et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en .iij. jors ou en .iiij.	And because of this, the ancient doctors commanded to leave the wound open until the danger of the illness passes. And once it has passed, after three or four days.
Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee;	And then they commanded to stitch up the wound and treat it, until it was healed;
et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist .i. coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon;	I saw a maiden take one dagger and plunged it into her neck, severing some of the veins near the collarbone.
et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	and I was called to treat her, and found her already dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood issuing from it, and indeed, there was no major vein or artery that led there but rather the windpipe, and the veins flowed through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee;	I acted quickly, and thus healed the wound, and treated it until it was cured;
et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition;	and there was nothing left for the maiden but that her voice became weak from speaking, and she returned after that to her duties;
por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	thus I declare that in tailoring the epiglottis, there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	In the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes;	Cysts in the throat are called "throat hernia", and they are large cysts of a blackish color, and are very common in women;
et est selonc .ij. manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	and according to two ways: natural and accidental; or naturally there is no organ.
Et li accidens est selonc .ij. manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere;	And the accidents are according to two ways, of which one is like pus from us, and the other way is like an abscess that comes from our artery;
et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire:	And there is fear, and it doesn't allow for big operations outside that in the one who is small, and it has been proven and searched through everything intrusive:
se tu le trueves ausi com .i. nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point;	if you find it as thin as a newborn calf, and cannot allow any vein to pierce, then treat it, just like one treats a calf wound, and apply all its remedies, if there is need for it;
et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	and search well soon, and treat it accordingly until it is completely healed.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances;	Many ways exist for us, of which I will mention all the similarities;
et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	And it is fitting that I describe all the differences that exist between us and dislocation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is characterized by heat and fever lasting until the body's fluids have disappeared and decay has occurred; then the fever and heat subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient .i. syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros;	With dislocation, there is no heat, fever or pain, and contains one pus sac which is its own bag, and is according to the color of the body, it begins also like a boil, and becomes large;
et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	And they depend on two appearances, or greasiness, or moisture, and no color are like as I described in the classification.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary when you come to the treatment of a new injury that you first try and inquire about all the tool which is called "the introducer", according to its form or chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme;	And the method of inquiring about the pus from wounds is that you take what is more moist than what you find inside the pus, and twist your fingers slightly and slightly, until you know that the tools have pierced the core, then do it according to the size of the pus.
puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	Then remove the introducer, and be careful not to let it jump out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes;	When moisture seeps through, whatever its color may be, if it enters as I have described for other abscesses;
et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout;	And if after the introduction of the probe no moisture comes, know that it is fatty, so cut it across, and take hold with tongs, and gently scrape it from each side, leaving the garment where it lies, which you should remove cleanly with a pincement.
et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	And if you cannot remove it cleanly, then remove it piece by piece so that nothing is left behind.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois;	Because if anything is left behind, it will recur through multiple occurrences;
et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez;	And if it stays a little while, and the loss doesn't trouble you, use powders that corrode when applied to wounds, and hold the wound still. Place things that soothe abscesses nearby, and treat other treatments until it heals completely;
et se li nous est grans, si cout les .ij. levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	And if it's large, cut the two edges of the wound, and treat whoever is bleeding inside.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the vein is larger than what is contrary or another thing that requires urgency, prepare the wound with vinegar and let it sit for two days or three days, until the wound heals from inside out. Then resume treating where you left off after removing the old material.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de .iij. manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a .iij. quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et .i. qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de .iij. manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule;	Here are the forms of the instruments for intervention, and there are three ways: large, medium, and small. And if you have four square ones which are called "albaret" and one which is called "breb". There are also three types in terms of size: large, medium, and small, to surround the abscesses of fistulas;
et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule;	And they are also like the needles from which one removes the thorns, and they are made of amber citrine, or iron, or silver, and yellow ones are more effective than black lead for enclosing abscess cavities.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	And they come in three ways: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the openings of the wounds.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures de .iij. manieres ausi;	The shapes of the hooks resemble sheep, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if the hooks have two swellings in three different ways, just like that.
et si a oncines qui ont .iij. corbeures, et sont ausi de .iij. manieres; et si a oncines qui ont .ij. corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de .iij. manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	And if the hooks have two swellings and are also in three ways; and if there are hooks with two swellings, single-hooked hooks, and these too are in three ways; and all of this is necessary according to their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf;	The head of this one that they make be sharp, and there are some who do not cut strength from both sides, of whom one sears the skin, for in such cases one does not encounter the vein nor the nerve.
et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes;	And of these introducers are the lancets placed in sleeves, so that the patient does not feel it when abscesses are opened.
et sont de .iij. manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois;	There are three ways: large, small, and medium, just as you see;
et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus;	and only use it with the inner arm for things like legs, arms, breasts, and similar body parts;
et aucune fois fait on .i. autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	And no other small instrument is made, resembling whips of thieves', according to this shape, to which one stops the blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And it is placed only once in its proper location among veins that are repaired and arteries, and never follows this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme;	Never do the breasts of some men swell when they begin to become corrupt, until they appear like breasts of women;
et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne b. jusques a .g.:	And remain ugly and swollen, and those who wish to cure them should do it according to this shape of the line b. up until g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee;	Then scrape off the fat, and apply medicine to the wound to promote healing, then join the two edges of the wound for stitching, and treat until it is fully healed;
et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en .ij. costelz desus, par .ij. semblans fendures;	And if the mammary gland is sagging down and shrunk by its size, similar to how it occurs in women when they are old or after childbirth, cut it into two halves above, making two apparent slits;
de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.;	From which one holds to the other at the end of each and both, so that the larger line contains the smaller according to this form, from this line b. until the line g.;
puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les .ij. levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Then scrape off the skin that is between the two edges, remove the fat, and follow what we have instructed about stitching and powders, as well as everything necessary for treatment until it is healed.

Those who do not have their penis in its place suffer blindness, because none give birth who have the penis at the tip of the penis; so they cannot urinate before lifting their penis up; and cannot impregnate either because the matter cannot reach to the spermatic substance, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez. de la circoncision	Concerning circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a continuation of other diseases; still, whenever we perform this act of our own will and for children, it must be done with the best work, and in the gentlest manner possible for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the old ones did not mention circumcision of their children, for they do not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	But I have wanted the majority of masters and lords who performed circumcision between the first day and one week, and during all infancy; it was the best because there are two layers there, and by chance, if one leaves this above and the other remains below.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	They recover with difficulty and the pain is doubled, and at the operation where the body is cut open, it's not clear exactly where the injury lies; and in the amputation of a bone by mistake the surgeon cuts the limb, and proceeds with the work, often performing amputations when they're unnecessary as I have noticed.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	From the operation which is performed to strengthen everything, I found that there are advantages to experimentation, because strength cuts as well above as below equally well.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en .i. tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues;	But when you press your hand, if it cuts equally in the middle, .i., all is tensed. Then let the bleeding continue for a while because this is the menses; and put powder here and there on top of the powder. Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape for the cleaning is this: let both ends be held and be sharp, and have the ends as large as the fingers evenly.

The error of world creation happens when the kidneys inside are disturbed during incision; therefore, it is necessary that you extend up to your fingernail, in such a way that they make an abscess; and do it evenly, and if you cannot hold up to your fingernail, then use tweezers, and then proceed.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they penetrate for three days, and the one which is beneath the penis is swollen, let him wait until the abscesses around it are alleviated, and gently scrape it; do it as much as you can move, and avoid touching the part of the penis, for it will not harm it.

dou retenement de l’urine	holding back of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division;	The retention of urine is due to the formation of stone, or frozen blood, or bladder obstruction, or a formed lump, or similar things that we mentioned in the section.
et se li urine n’est desliie, et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e;	And if the urine is released and you see retention due to stone in the bladder or neck of the bladder, it is necessary that the patient be supported on his knees. des maladies de la vessie	On diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When burns or blood come to the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled there, and you see distilled waters and medicines, then have all the instrument called 'clepsidra', and it has this form:

de la piere	from the stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have discussed the methods of stone division and extraction together with medicines; and we have spoken about the difference between indwelling stones and those in the kidney, as well as all the signs, and when one should operate on a stone; and in the bladder, and in the penis; and I will clearly and briefly tell you.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that stones which are indwelling in the bladder occur more often among children, and this is a sign that the infection jumps from the bladder akin to an infection that manifests through subtlety; they open the urethra, and rub the patient's penis, and he urinates many times, and then it gets caught. And at these jumps of the stone, its base can be found; and for several months, children's healing is light until they reach four years old, it causes much discomfort in the elderly, and occurs in middle age, to those who are between adulthood and old age; and the treatment for those with large stones is lighter than for those with small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines. Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere. par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere. dou fremit	with trembling

des plaies	from wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have spoken about the treatment of wounds in the division; now we will discuss treatments for hands and medicine according to their completion.

Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses;	The things by which wounds are made come from being hit by a stone, and the size of a sword or knife, or by spear or staff or axe, or by similar things;

Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans,	I say that when a simple wound comes or a joint is involved, and the bone is not broken, be cautious whether it's due to stone or similar matters, and the skin has been completely torn apart and the wound is large,

Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon .ij. parties; chalz vive .iij. parties, et le poudre subtilment,	And the method of preparing this powder is as follows: take a part of incense; dragon's blood .ii parts; living charcoal .iii parts, and finely ground it,

et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And bind it well, and let her rest without straining, if she doesn't swell; one removes the medicine only when she is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	Only this is done with salt alone, when one doesn't have the incense or the blood of the dragon, but only when the art has healed the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre;	And if the art (skill or medicine) has healed the wound, even then, don't use this powder;
mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe;	But apply on some well-prepared poultices, or oat flour mixed with water and honey, as long as it emits a boil;
puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then proceed with other treatments until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz;	And if bone fracture accompanies the wound and it's small, one should use delicate forceps to attempt its realignment.
et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And I will tell you about fractures of the skull after this.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound at the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	This wound comes from the neck and it is simple, if there is no difference between it and those at the head, but if a nerve in the neck or an artery has been cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire;	If it's a nerve, then there is no other remedy but to leave the wound open, and not to put anything restraining in it, for it damages nerves and causes their regression;
et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres;	And do not put anything cold on the wound, because the substance of nerves is cold, and the continuation of such things is with the brain, which is the highest member;
mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce,	but use the medicine nearby, such as charcoal washed in gentle water and mixed with rose oil, and also wash the cloth in gentle water.
et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	and other mineral stones in this manner, and moist applications.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, bind it with strips and then treat it until it heals.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu;	And if the wounds are deep and full of pus, then puncture or even deeper.
et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est;	And if an artery is cut, and blood starts flowing out, then you must uncover it, straighten it, and if necessary, cauterize.
et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va,	And if the throat is cut, or the knees, then you must keep the flow path, through which the meat goes.
si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel;	If you heat it on the base of the throat, and do not touch the throat but adjust it according to its natural shape;
et puis l’estrain avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez;	and then apply the dressing, and let it be for several days, then treat with drying ointments until it heals;
et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier;	and if there is an indentation in the bone due to the wound, operate;
et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse,	and if there are fragments of bone, remove them if you can, and leave those that you cannot retrieve until the wound heals;
et soit desevree et aligie li issue;	and let it be released and healed by its own nature;
et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	and if the wound is fresh, apply the powder I have mentioned on it.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as instructed in my chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from lance or knife wounds
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz;	If it's a spear wound or from a knife and the injury is deep, then if you notice that wind can easily flow out of the wound without resistance from the body tissues, then you understand that the wound is fatal.
et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont,	and if it's not deep and is full of blood throughout when fresh, then don't put any powder on it or bind it up right away; let the blood drain completely without obstruction until the first hour.
et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide;	and let him rest with his body, and keep him occupied so he doesn't move around.
mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie .ij. fois le jor;	but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day.
et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor,	And if you don't have oil, put old cotton into the wound to absorb moisture.
et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie .iij. jors, ou .iiij., ou plusors;	And make the patient rest on the wound for 3 days, or 4, or more if needed.
si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’es traingnemens d’alainne;	If there is no seizure, nor harmful trembling of the heart, nor single convulsions;
et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	And when you see good conditions, know that the wound has been saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez;	Treat with various remedies until there is no more bloodshed;
et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	and if it does not heal and work, know that there will be an open wound; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant;	And if the wound is from a sword or knife cut, whether it is simple or worse or on the back, treat as the one in front would.
s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez;	If it's large, stitch it; and if it's small, use powder; and if it's deep in the bone or has broken pieces inside, clean the wound and remove any foreign objects.
et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions;	And if they are not evacuated, let the wound fester, assisting with extractions if needed.
et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And for other wounds on other members, the judgments are similar as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from the rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis;	The ruptures of the belly can be large, medium-sized, and small;
de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus;	In a major injury, one can sometimes see parts of the intestines, or the entrails, due to their exposure.
et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans,	Sewing up injuries is more difficult and, in no case, is it better than treating a small wound compared to a large one,
por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut;	Therefore, when we attempt to sew back the intestines in place, if they are not carefully and progressively placed;
por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes,	Because the intestines swell up soon after feeling cold, thus they cannot be sewn back too tightly;
et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres .ij.	And because of this we must treat the wound, for thus we massage the intestines to their place that they are in others.
Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc .iiij. manieres:	Know that the rupture of the belly occurs according to four ways:
les .ij. costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre,	The two common sutures occur in the abdominal stitch,
et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et .ij. autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies;	and other stitches from wounds to the body and two other specific stitches are common for other injuries;
et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	And yet they are more fitting with the stitch of the belly, and I will say each one and clarify.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer,	I say that when the wound is small, and nothing from the intestine sticks out,
et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des .ij. manieres:	And it's possible to heal like this, one of these two ways:
ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit,	or by the smallness of the wound, as we have said,
ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	Because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere:	And when it is cold, warm it in this manner:
moillie une esponge ou .i. mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement,	Moisten a sponge or one-third of a cloth only in water.
ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique,	or you cook in water with vinegar and cypress and spikes,
et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee;	And let the intestine grow as long as the womb is opened;
et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And do not restrain this wine at all times, and wait until you feel it beginning to relieve.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites,	And when you see the swelling leave, if you moisten the intestine with water or broth that has been cooked well,
car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose;	because through this way, the entry accepts little food.
et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes;	And if it cannot enter, they make a slight incision with the tool used to remove the warts;
et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille,	And the first treatment is to let the cut heal,
que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait;	that we should not cut it without great necessity or if it's not needed;
et c’est li estrumens por le fendre:	and this is the instrument to split it with:
si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	if you cut within the curve and not outside, and see this shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer,	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines jump out,
si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre,	if you put them back according to their natural shape in its proper place,
se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	and if possible, for this is worth moving.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre,	When the wound is large, and it's situated below the belly,
si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos,	it's necessary that you let the patient lie on his back,
et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief;	and place his legs higher than his head;
et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre,	and if it's in the abdominal region,
si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz,	Place the head and buttocks higher than the body parts below.
et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des .ij. parties	And also if there is a rupture of the abdomen in one of the two parts.
si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre;	So ensure that the elevated part of the intestines is higher than the other.
et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And in this way, it is appropriate to apply what I have said about large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet,	Small wounds are treated with what you have provided,
puis aies entre tes mains .i. ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main,	Then have in your hands... I. Minister pity who heals all the rupture at his hand,
et assemble les levres;	and bring together the lips;
et c’est la maniere commune de costures,	And this is the common way of suturing,
et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie,	and it consists in you using a needle or more, depending on the size of the wound's width,
puis laisse des le chief de la plaie .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait .i. boin fil fort;	then start from the edge of the wound one digit's width in, and place a needle with one good strong thread;
et perce les .ij. chiés dou cuir avec les .ij. chiés dou siphac,	and pierce both the skin layers with both the needle threads from the flesh,
qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie,	which is beneath the skin as long as you pierce it from that part,
et assemble les .ij. chief dou siphac les .iiij. ensamble;	and join the two main sections of the siphon with the three together;
puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de .ij. pars,	then sew them using a doubled thread around the needle on both sides,
puis assemble les .ij. chiés de la plaie avenanment,	and join the two edges of the wound with stitches,
et puis laisse .i. doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille;	And then leave out one and a half inches, and insert another needle;
puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille,	then weave the thread as you did with the first needle,
et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles,	and continue doing so according to what you know about needles,
tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte;	until the entire wound is restrained;
et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses,	And let there be needles of medium size, between fine and thick ones,
car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer:	For the thin needles cut all the flesh, and the very thick ones can't enter well at all:
por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes;	Because it is necessary for them to be of medium size;
et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir,	and it's not right to have needles sticking too far out from the flesh and the skin,
k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure;	They do not cut and open the wound before the stitch;
et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir,	and then remove the needles, so they don't irritate the patient when sleeping,
et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir,	and cover the needles with cloths or bandages to keep them clean,
et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee;	and leave it until the wound is stitched together;
et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies,	And this method of sewing with needles is more applicable to small wounds,
car il i soffist une aguille ou .ij.	because it requires one needle or two.
Li seconde costure si est commune,	The second type of stitch is common,
et est que tu assemble les .ij. chiés dou cuir et les .ij. chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait .i. fort fil moien;	And the second stitch involves assembling two leather threads and two silk threads, which are then assembled onto one needle with a strong thread in the middle;
et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz .iiij. ensamble,	And when you have pierced these shoulders all together,
si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras;	then remove the needle from the spot where you started piercing, in the manner one would cut threads;
et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi;	and leave a space between each stitch as big as a small coin;
ceste costure sevent li home,	these stitches should be even across the entire piece.
et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre,	And I treat a wound where one has lost an organ or has a stomach issue,
qui estoit navrez d’un coutel,	who had been cut by a knife,
et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant,	and the wound was larger than a hand's breadth,
et issoit des intestines bien .ij. palmes de grant,	and it was the size of two handbreadths for the intestines,
et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	And the wound was within the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit .xxiiij. houres fuer,	I brought back his intestine, and it had been out for twenty-one hours.
et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a .xv. jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	And the wound healed up to fifteen days, and I treated it, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle;	And they had judged that he was going to die, and it was a miracle;
et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en .i. leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines;	And I would not treat it with ointment, for I was in a place where none could be found, nor any medicine;
et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel .ij. fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And I would change the cloth on the wound two times a day, and wash it with honey water until it was clean.
Or vos dirai les .ij. propres manieres de cousture:	I will tell you the two proper methods of sewing:
pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens;	Take the needle, and place it on the outer part up to that inner side;
quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille,	When it has pierced the artery straight on, if you place the head of the syphilitic or costive disease where you have inserted the needle,
et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer;	and make it pierce from another side through the inner part up to that which is on the outside;
et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz,	and when you hear about this seam, it is like threading with a tailor would sew fur.
et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	and leave the siphac on one side once, and take it from another until the seam is fully accomplished.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement,	The second method of stitching, as Galen properly stated,
si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les .ij. parties ensamble naturelment,	If it is done like everyone else does, by joining the two parts together naturally,
et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere:	And apply one to the tip of the other, in such manner:
fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement,	Stitch with a needle or the tip of a near finger, and make it pierce only the upper one,
et laisse les .ij. chiés dou syfac;	and let both of the shoulder joints be warm;
puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens,	then turn the needle and make it pierce from the outer part until it reaches inside.
as .ij. chiés dou syfac;	as both shoulder joints are warm;
puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en .ij. autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit;	then pierce each from the outer part until it reaches inside, using two other warm shoulder joints that are on the opposite side;
et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	And this is the clumsy way of sewing up and the most common one.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent,	Galien taught this word, and none testify it,
c’on doit coudre le ventre a .ij. aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune;	One must stitch the abdomen with two needles, or where there is thread in each one;
et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies;	And one should insert one needle from one side and the other from the other, like those who stitch metals.
et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre,	and know that when the rupture is within the belly,
si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	then the stitch is more serious than in other parts of the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies:	The judgement of the wound is like that of the judgement of other wounds:
et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee,	and it's thus when you find the fresh wound completely filled with blood, just as the art has made it.
si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char,	if you set it back near the intestine, and at the wound; then place the stimulating powder above.
et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe;	and if there has been a scar, apply any available ointment until the wound heals;
et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach;	and sew with thread, ensuring that the stitches are even and neat.
puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez;	then treat the wound in the same manner as others, until it is healed.
et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel,	And if you do not have medicine, place it on top, as soon as it starts to bleed, use old cotton.
et le remue .ij. fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	and move it twice a day until it becomes healthy.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples;	For you don't need other medicines in various preparations when the wounds are simple;
et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz,	and if you doubt that the wound will cause communication with essential members,
si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset,	It is necessary for you to moisten a thread lightly in oil of warmed heat, or in rose-scented oil.
et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles;	And put it inside the joints, and over the armpits;
et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient,	and if there is pain or gangrene in the bowels, and it happens often,
si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine;	if black wine enemas are administered, and especially if gangrene has reached up to the intestine;
et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	And pierce within, and know that when it's large intestine, it is easier to heal than the smaller ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez,	The intestine known as "young" cannot be healed once it is damaged,
et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	And this is due to the location of the veins and the subtlety of the entire body, as well as its approach towards its own nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres;	And if the boil leaps out from the wound, then it is treated again as with an intestine, while it's still fresh;
et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne,	And if it is old and turned towards or black in color, you should tie the black part of it, so that no bleeding occurs from there.
car il i a voinnes et arteres;	because there are veins and arteries;
puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien,	then cut what is between the ligament,
et met les .ij. chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	and place both shoulders hanging down from the part over the wound up to beyond it for easing the extraction when the cartilage closes them, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	From the rupture of the boil
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite,	When the intestinal contents spill out, and the wound is small,
si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes,	If one could return it to any condition,
por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance;	Because I've seen that the abdomen of someone pierced by a spear can become swollen;
et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac,	The injury was located on the right side of the stomach,
et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez;	And it became inflamed and developed into a fistula, causing malaise and flatulence;
je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	I applied treatment according to my ability, and continued refining it until the patient was healed, and sealed the wounds.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre;	And when I saw the wound healed, I was uncertain if there might be internal injuries in their abdomen;
et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans;	And there was no harm, but it stayed in much better conditions, eating and drinking;
et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere:	And they told some experimenters that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be treated in this manner:
pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie,	take large pieces of flesh, then join the edges of the wound,
et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les .ij. levres,	and when the flesh has opened its mouth, place it against the two lips,
si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus;	If she forces her mouth up;
et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier,	and then she holds the head in place, so that it cannot be released;
puis met .i. autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise;	then applies another strain in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely treated;
et cout la plaie.	and heals the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide,	Those who are overly zealous in their intestines, and do not cause any harm to the patient,

de l’aposteme de l’ungle	From the abscess of the nail

la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	The pain deepens in the hand.

Des vils	Of low quality
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors;	Vessels are thick-walled and filled with surplus melancholic substances that originate from various parts of the body;

De la voinne civile	From the civil vein
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor;	This vein is confined in legs, in warm areas where no herbs nor trees grow, and in ground with no moisture;

Des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	Worms that are born between the skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués,	This illness is called in our land "cattle disease", because it occurs frequently to cattle,
et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant,	and it's a small worm that hatches between the skin and flesh, traveling throughout the body both upwards and downwards,
et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer;	And you can feel it well by touching each part of the body, as far as the skin goes, and jumps out;
et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre;	And it is affected by corruption of some fluids, if they come towards worms, snakes and roundworms or in the stomach;
et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil,	And there is doubt about its nature, because when it travels through the body, and ascends to the head, and reaches the eye,
par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	Perhaps it enters and destroys the eye; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait:	When you see it being treated and drained, one cannot help but note when it will:
si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement,	so it follows that you should tie the joint above and below with a strong bandage tightly,

si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire;	if you need to use a fire cautery over it, until it stops bleeding;
