et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer;	And if you see it coming close to your head near the eye, hold steady over him with your finger, then lift up and pull strongly.
et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries,	It is necessary to use the application of purification from bodily fluids through medicines in solution for the ailments caused by humoral imbalances,
et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	And if meat causes putrefaction when eaten.
De la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres,	This disease is called in our land "vakirir", and it is a pain that comes to any limbs,
et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	And it spreads from limb to limb; and I have seen what I am telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais;	I was called to attend a woman in distress, and she showed me her arms, and I saw a small swelling in the vein of the arm;
et .i. poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule,	And one or two days later, the wound ascends as if a worm at the shoulder,
plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre;	Sooner than anything else, like hot silver when it is cut off from its source;
li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule,	The pain leaves that side and enters the shoulder,
et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais;	And then a little later it spread throughout the body, until it reached the other arm;
puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	Then I was told she twisted inside the body, just as I saw.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled much how she moved from limb to limb in this way, for I had never seen this disease carried out like this before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre,	Anyway, I have seen many times that well people would move their pain to another part of the body,
mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme;	but I had never seen such a thing like this in a woman;
et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes,	And I thought it was because of this that the woman had smooth skin, and her veins exposed,
et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte;	And because of this appears that constrained wind;
et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	And do not perceive according to this reason among those who are delicate, and have wet bodies and veins that respond.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit,	And when you see treat this illness, and if the patients feel pain, if it opens up as we have said,
si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer;	if it opens both upwards and downwards quickly, and then stops until that constrained wind within the body comes out;
et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz,	And apply the cautery to it; and if you cannot see it by your eyes,
si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	if you are treating someone who suffers from wind disorders, such as foul pills and Serapis' pills, and similar sorts.
Des saiettes	Of arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows vary according to their shape and the location of their impact on the body.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees;	The variety among them is such that there are those with large points, and small ones, and hairy, and fused;
et de celles qui ont .ij. angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces;	and of those that have two angles, and of those that have tongues, and of those where there are pieces;
et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc .ij. manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit,	and the one that urinates in no member but does so according to two ways: or through the main body,
si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	or like the brain, heart, liver, kidneys, bladder, intestines, and similar organs.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent:	When it comes to dislocation, then indeed not at all any part of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, becomes evident:
si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions;	It is necessary that you be prepared for the extraction of this arrow, because death comes after in various circumstances;
et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	And when that bad sign does not appear and the arrow has not been fully extracted, you should pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil,	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, causing the fluid that is under the brain to escape,
est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole;	When there is blindness and swelling and redness in the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and convulsions and confusion of intellect, and vomiting of bile;
et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix;	and perhaps there is loss of smell or hearing; and sometimes he loses speech and voice.
et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char;	and the wound becomes moist with white pus resembling maggots, and it also appears like burned flesh;
et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	and if this sign is visible, you should continue with the treatment, and remove the arrow if it's still there.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide;	The sign of the arrow when it hits or pierces the heart is that it is close to the left breast, and also feels as if it were stuck in something hard, not empty;
et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope:	And by chance the arrow may also remain silent like the pulse, and in black blood, and causes coldness and cold sweat, and fainting:
saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	So, with no doubt, know that death approaches.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that never leaves is that there's no foam spill from the wound, and the throat swells up, and the patient's skin changes color, and they sigh loudly with a chill in their breath.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow closes in the thigh's covering, it affects the small bones; and there is great pain and great distress, with sighing; and they move all their limbs from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow penetrates or touches the stomach, by chance it leaps out of the wound without digesting any substance.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if the arrow penetrates or touches the belly, and leaps out without passing through any intestines, then there is no hope for treatment, nor in the extraction of the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if the arrow pierces the bladder and urine flows out and escapes, causing severe pain to the patient: you must know that the wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other body parts, such as the arm and neck and throat and shoulder and shoulder blade and elbow and collarbone and ribs and back muscles, and thighs, and similar limbs are safe according to many dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the muscle or artery and it's not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because when you do something else.
Il avint a .i. home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis:	It happened that at two in the morning, an arrow struck him in the side of his thigh at the knee joint:
je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	I tried it and moved her across under the ear's fat, and felt nothing unusual.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz,	And in one game an arrow, as it falls into the grease of the eye beneath the paper beneath,
et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust,	And the arrow was returned, and one could only touch its tip towards the shaft,
et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout .i. fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And the arrow was large as one might find on a Turkish bow, weighing just slightly over half a pound without including feathers; the game was fair, and no unfortunate incidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles:	And I aimed an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and this arrow had feathers:
je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I shaved them, trimmed until I was satisfied with my work, and made sure they pleased the Christians.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit;	And drew out an arrow from one's body or stomach, that it was embedded inside, and I thought he would die;
et puis qu’il ot passez .xxx. jors, si ne mua point sa disposition;	and after thirty days had passed, if its position did not change;
je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I cut into the arrow, I fitted it with a mechanism, and I pulled it out, without any bad incident.
Et si vis .i. home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus;	And if you see one or two arrows hit or pierce someone, and found the wound healed above;
et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez,	and keeps the arrow inside, without altering its natural disposition,
ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	nor finds any harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis .i. autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie;	And see one other person, who was struck by an arrow on their face, and found the wound healed;
et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And thus one endures great pain; and no other similar symptoms.
Et traï une saiette a .i. home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz,	And took an arrow from one and a half homes of the princes' king, which was stuck in his thigh.
et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue	and it was slightly tilted towards the right side; and the arrow had been fully inserted.
Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue .iij. jors. Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I was summoned for the treatment after it had happened for three days. I found the wound to be very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie;	I tried to understand its entire delicate attempt, but did not feel it;
et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	and there was pain and discomfort all over his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette	I thought it was from the tip of the dart.
Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast;	I put an adhesive plaster on his ear because the ear did not swell;
et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	And I saw the head of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens,	I applied the healing salve for several days, and quickly resolved the wound, then let the patient rest for a long time.
tant qu’il sentit la saiette .i. jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	Until he sensed the arrow within his nose; and he told me about it.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte,	I applied corrosive ague medicine to the wound for several days until it was opened.
et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu;	And tried, and felt the head of the arrow which was piercing at its base;
puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement;	then adjusted through the opening of the wound using this medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared visibly;
et trespassa bien li termines entor .iiij. mois,	and passed well inside for about four months,
et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir;	then I opened the wound properly so that I could spread the tweezers, and pulled on it from both sides, but it wouldn't come out;
adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris .i. jor as tenailles bien faites,	Therefore never cease refining and engineering ways to create tools until I took the first one, a pair of well-made tweezers, for use.
selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	Following what its shape will bring to the end of this chapter, until I treat it, and will repair the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer:	And those who examine believe that the cartilage at the nose cannot be restored:
je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	So I treated it accordingly, and healed the wound, and restored the health of the patient completely.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes,	You have been told about the nature of extracting some arrows,
si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre;	so that you place your treatment on what I do not say, for the books cannot take in everything;
mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant,	but listen well to a small part of my masters' wisdom, and about what is here and lacking;
trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	test true knowledge or nine works, and the ninth tool, for the removal of things that occur in this craft.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc .ij. manieres:	I say that arrows do not stay within the limbs where they are embedded thus:
ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part;	or by entering through their length, or from another side;
et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	And the one that jumps in when it enters or when it is embedded, this arrow penetrates into their flesh, and does so no matter if it happens once now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue;	And if it doesn't jump in now, leave her until the body is thoroughly cooked internally, and allow for the juices to come out.
et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor;	And similarly if it's stuck in the bone, and can't come out, leave it like that for several days, and remove a little each day;
et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout .i. foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And then it jumps out, and if it doesn't jump out, puncture through with a small hole for all one inch, until the depth of the lesion is widened, and then remove it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil,	And if the arrow is stuck in the bone at the neck, going up to one of the brain's chambers,
et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors,	and all the accidents that I have mentioned appear to the patient: if he does not treat it immediately, but leaves it until it is even after a few days,
car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	For if the arrow comes just to the shaft, this is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac,	And if the arrowhead has only pierced into the bone and does not come up to the shaft,
et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	and remains with no harm to the patient for a few days without any mishap, if it is well removed.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is so deeply embedded and cannot come out, then administer warm baths internally, as I have told you; then treat the wound until it heals properly.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente;	And if the arrow is returned to its original place inside the body so that you can't see it anymore, then seek it out with all your effort;
et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble;	and if you feel it, then guide it with any suitable instrument;
et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette,	and if you cannot do so due to the tightness of the wound, and because of the depth of the arrow,
et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans;	and if there is no bone, nerve, or vein, then cut as long as the wound becomes large;
et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient,	and pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are ears attached to it that she holds,
si oste la char qui est ens fichie de .ij. pars au mues que tu pues,	if you can remove the bone which is stuck in at two points by its length that you can handle,
et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire;	and then break or bend the ears of the arrow as long as you can pull it out;
et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	do this carefully so that you don't break the arrow, making its removal easier.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you can't do it all at once, if until the middle of your arm is still sore, then try again, because the extraction will be easy.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre;	And if the recurrent bleeding goes against you, proceed with what we have instructed about treatment in this chapter;
et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril,	and be cautious of incising near nerves and veins, and take care to draw out the arrow without risk,
ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens,	or quickly or gently, firmly or skillfully; and adjust the patient according to the shape they were in when the arrow struck them.
car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	Because it is the greatest help possible for you, and if you cannot do it, then place him according to what the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment:	The arrow that comes from another side, or if it exposes any part of the body, or if the skin is swollen in such a way that you can see or feel it clearly:
taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Cut there up until your tongs can take it, and then extract it. If it jumps now, do so immediately.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if she is caught in the bone, twist your hand around it until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer;	And if it cannot come out, she/he should still allow it to remain there, and then continue the extraction until it comes forth forcibly.
et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust;	and if it is an arrow that is in him, he removes all of the shaft;
et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre .i. estrument cheveit,	And if it's a child who's affected, and you see them requiring treatment with a bone extractor, then administer one bone instrument to them.
si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer,	so that the tip of the arrow goes into the opening of the tool; and then push it forcefully,
et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute .i. estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if he has an arrow stuck in him, take one sharp tool to help remove it.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues,	And if the arrow touches his skin, you should cut all the flesh around or where it pierces, if you can.
puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	Then treat the wound as is appropriate.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope;	And if the arrow hits or pierces in the chest or stomach or bladder or ribs and is close to vital organs, and you can access it, then cover up, if you can.
et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est;	And protect yourself from cutting the vein and the nerve, and then you remove it, and then suture the wound if this task is required;
et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And continue with treatment until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used for arrows is similar to the beak of a bird, and here is the shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And in terms of size they are as follows: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel,	The shape of the terminal hair is also like the feathers of a bird,
por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	because it points at the tip of the arrow, as this is its form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The shape for gripping and pulling like tongs is thus:
des voinnes dou cors communes	from the veins of common horns
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont .xxxi., de coi il a ou chef xvi.,	Of veins through which we cleanse ourselves are thirty-one, from which there are sixteen,
c’est a savoir: .ij. batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»;	This means:
et les .ij. arteres qui sont en .ij. temples apparans;	And the two arteries that are in the two visible temples;
et .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers des .ij. eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»;	And two veins that are in the two eyelids of the two eyes, which are called 'aspirers';
et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis;	And the vein that is inside the forehead; and the vein that is on the head under the nose;
et les .ij. guindeges qui sont ou col;	and the two jugulars which are at or around the collarbone;
et les .ij. voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»;	and the two veins that are in the cheeks above the mouth, and these are the veins that are called "aughers";
et .ij. voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont .v. en chescun bras:	The veins that we commonly heal are five in each arm:
l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»;	One is the cephalic vein, and it runs under the left rib, and they call this "the arm vein";
et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique,	And the median one is called "the fast" and consists of the cephalic vein and the basilic vein,
et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit,	And they call it "the heart vein"; and the basilic vein is either under or on the right rib.
et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile,	And they call this condition "the vein of the belly", and it is located on the flank,
et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	and this is the one that heals, which opens clearly on the sack.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a .ij. rains;	And the salve area is the vein located between the index and ring fingers, and it extends to two inches;
et en la jambe et ou piet sont .iij. voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit,	and on the leg and at the heel are three veins: one is below the bend of the thigh, on the left side of the body;
et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei;	And the second bone which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called "nurse", which is in the ankle of the other side.
et en l’autre jambe sont .iij. voinnes desoz celles.	And in the other leg are three veins beneath those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine;	The health of the veins that are after the ears helps with catarrhs and migraines;
et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide,	And the qualities of the healer, as I have told you, is that you smell the head of the sick person,
et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis,	And rub the arm or the veins with a rough cloth; then pinch the patient's neck to one side,
tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en .ij. leus dependens dou chief:	until you see the two veins behind the ears in each of the two arms depending on the head:
quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche;	then place your hand there, and where you feel the pulse under your hand, gently guide it;
puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont,	then take the scalpel, and insert it along the vein until you reach the bone, then lift your hand all the way up to the vein above.
et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien .ij. dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues;	And cut and let the skin and the vein well two inches deep, and make blood come out until you see;
puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee;	then tighten and bind it, as long as it is healed;
et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	and I have already spoken of the incision and the cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des .ij. arteres que sont en .ij. temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene,	The health of the two arteries that are in the two temples is like an old maid,
et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz;	And indeed, with ointment for the eyes acquainted, and on the body of febrile tears the eyes act.
et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis:	And that quality of the physician is such as I say:
et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les .ij. voinnes aperent apertement;	And it happens that the patient stretches his neck, so that the two veins can be seen clearly;
et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche;	and feel the pulse over your two arms, and then judge by this;
puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz,	Then lift your hand above the vein near your thumb tip, and hold the scalpel steady,
et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en .ij. autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit;	and lift the vein upwards, and cut it, just like you did in other veins, and let blood flow according to your need;
puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton;	then release the patient, place your thumb on the vein for an hour, then put cotton there.
et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	And then let it form, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of this before concerning its development and extraction, or the start of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor;	The drainage of the vein on the forehead is as valuable as that of the superficial temporal artery among ancient diseases and migraines, and for flushing.
et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere;	And its quality is that the patient twists his neck in order to relieve the pain until the vein appears;
puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	Then take the tool known as "awl", which has this shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues;	And place the tip on the vein, and apply pressure with your hand or another object, and allow blood to flow according to the amount you can see.
puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	then release the neck of the patient, and tie the vein as long as it remains healthy and no cut is made with a flame that could widen it.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Every vein, it must not be too close with the flames; and the cut should be clean from side to side, because bone is nearby, and by chance the flames could break when they are thin.
Li sainie des .ij. voines que sont en .ij. larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice;	The healing of the two veins that are in the eyelids helps with eye issues, and at the nose, and at the cheek, and in the ear canal, and for face diseases;
et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant;	And the quality of their healing is such that the patient twists his neck by binding some tie, as before;
puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	Then let the healing take place, and make the healing pass through, somewhat like a long flame slightly wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle and should break by chance; then make correction with blood, as much as you need to, and then bind it with cotton, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice,	The healing of the vein near the nose is good for fever, and after full recovery, and diseases of the face,
si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene;	As when there is migraine and swelling that appears on the face, and similarly when it becomes old;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre,	And concerning health, if the patient constricts their throat, then they strain their nose with your left hand;
et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les .ij. narines,	And take a long fine flame, and place it between the two nostrils in the space on the lip;
car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre;	For the nostril does not open properly like that, and now the air will begin to pass through it;
et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree;	And don't go too fast, and adjust with your need for blood flow, then leave it for a night, as it is very quickly restored;
et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des .ij. guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes;	The health of the two kidneys aids in the tightening of the liver and the beginning of fermentation, and much illness, and pus formation, and corrosion, and herpes, and ulcers;
et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit;	And the quality of health is such that diseases constrain their neck on both sides, as we have said;
et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus .i. siege,	And let the masters stay on top of the head of the patient, and the patient lies down for one siege,
puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est;	then make a vein long somewhat wider, then drain blood moderately, or as much as is needed;
puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement,	then do the same with another vessel, then untie the knot, and press moderately on the vessels.
que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	so that the patient doesn't suffocate; and leave it until morning, so that the wound heals.
De la sainie des leivres	Of the health of the liver
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the veins in the mouth helps to form within the mouth, and leads to gum deterioration, and裂s in lips, and nosebleeds.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit;	And the quality of health consists in making the patient lie before you, and restraining his neck as I have said;
puis torne la levre, et regarde as .ij. voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre,	Then turn the mouth, and look at the two veins, one is on the right lip and the other on the left.
et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires:	And you can recognize them by their being black, and by the fact that inside they have small black veins:
cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance,	Treat both accordingly, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt,
si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des .ij. voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	If you treat the largest of each part, and do likewise with the two veins above and below, for this is the same method.
De la sainie desoz la lengue	From the treatment under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche;	The healing of veins located around the tongue is assisted after the healing of the capillary [perhaps meaning superficial or minor blood vessels], and this occurs in constriction of the throat. It addresses illnesses of the cornea, and illnesses of the mouth;
et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire:	The quality of the surgeon is such that the patient's body should feel the warmth of your hands in front of the sun, and lift their tongue. Look underneath on each side; there is a black vein:
saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Then heal both equally, but do not overheat them either, because beneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc .ij. manieres:	The veins of the arm that are commonly treated, are healed according to two methods:
ou em poignant a tout .i. flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»;	Let the flames of all one candle be large, or an olive slender like knives, and named "anesil";
et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	And they are large and slender according to the width and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the mirthin flame is much renowned, and it is quite wide as you see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble;	It serves to open the large veins filled with visibly abundant blood, and those containing much thickened blood;
et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	and this is the shape of an olive oil flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more delicate and pointed, and it is for purifying small veins or minor blood that is yellow.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre;	The purification of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that affect the throat, and the neck, and the lungs, and the abdomen;
et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	And it is for the surgeon to purify carefully, and to be aware of the artery that is nearby.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit;	And if blood flow has stopped due to a clot, and if bleeding occurs, then it is necessary to stop the bleeding, as I have said.
et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	and should not be held over the flame but trimmed like for rabbits.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre;	And if the basilica is not clearly opening, it is necessary to extract it, and replace with another one;
ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement;	Or you want no part of this, or you repair the vein by placing it under the arm: it opens clearly.
et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And the treatment for a flame-cautery, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz;	And if you are familiar with the location of the heart, it must be thus: you should straighten the arm and touch the area where you know the pulse;
puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil;	then mark the location of the collarbone, and then hold the arm in place, and treat with a flame cautery at that site;
et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	and watch out not to pierce the artery when you see the pulse area swell, for that is an artery: be careful and avoid it then.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere:	And if you see it protruding up as much as urine from a child, and the veins are red and delicate, know that this is blood from an artery:
haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient;	Hurry then, and place your finger for a long time, then hold your finger in place until the wound stops bleeding, as this has happened many times;
se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	Tie the arm down and leave it like that, do not move the patient's hand; be cautious and do not move them until they recover.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the wound does not stop bleeding and it takes time, and you lack the medicine, if you detect a blood vessel that is open, do so because the head retreats; and stop the bleeding on the wound.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor;	And take a peel of fig, cut it, and take one half and bind it well up to the other joint;
se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc;	If there's no bleeding, that's fine; if not, treat it as we have said, with powders that stop the blood;
et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And the bandages should not be too tight for the smallness of the wound and the strength of attaching the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz,	The healing of the vein in the middle is aided by treating blood from above and below it.
por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit;	Because she is made up of the basilica and cephalic parts, as we have said;
et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf,	And it is necessary for the surgeon to be aware of the nerve that is underneath, and if he does not go far enough, and he finds the nerve,
et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner;	And it swells and the health gets hurt, and by chance cannot be cured;
et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	And this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any due to its subtlety, then it is necessary for you to heal the wound with an artery saw before. And listen to the nerve with your touch.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two legs, make a cut long through it.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz;	The healing of the occipital sinus if it helps, that it has blood flowing down to the head, and helps with eye issues;
et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And it is necessary to heal at the oil flame or at the mint flame, for this is the safest of all veins, as it does not have a nerve or artery nearby.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence;	Always, seek to apply the lightest weight, and don't be discouraged if it needs to be done twice, and you repeat it;
et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	And by chance the arms of some people swell up, until one needs to do it for the first time, but they feel no pain.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit,	The first thing you should know about being a surgeon is that medicine is practiced only for the purpose of preserving health,
et por eschuir les maladies a venir;	and to avoid future diseases;
et soit li sainie faite en l’une des .iij. voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique;	And let the healing be done in one of the three veins which are or cut: that is to say, the cephalic vein, the femoral vein, and the basilic vein;
et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent;	And one should heal during the beginning of prayers on their knees, and in autumn and after winter after eating, when the sign of fullness is evident;
et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés .ij. houres ou .iij. dou jor.	And one should heal on the first or third day, after two hours or three days.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens;	The healing for diseases does not have a determined time, but only when need is of day or need, in all hours and at all times;
et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a .xiiij. ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	And it is not suitable to heal children until they are twelve years old, nor a pregnant woman only for a quarter of the months until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Neither should one heal an old person who has passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier,	And when anyone wishes to be healed, in whatever manner that may be, it is necessary for them to cleanse the intestines with a gentle purgative,
s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz;	if he has retained urine, so that the arteries pull away the superfluities causing harm to the main parts;
ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques;	Neither does it heal well those who are too overfed with meats, nor those who are drunk, as long as they have strength, nor the elderly.
et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors;	And if someone becomes unwell after colic pain, vomiting, abdominal cramps, frequent urination in women, and the stress from work, staying awake, or sexual activity, as well as when too much medicine or something from a weapon or injury;
puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir;	Then refine the bodily fluids; if someone is overweight due to food and drinks and medicine, then you should consider their tolerance.
puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc,	Then in or with a bath, if no harmful thing is found, for refining the blood,
et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit;	And heal from the wound down to the belly just past the third quarter, as we have said;
et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses;	And guard that day of labor and pain, and excess, and such like things;
et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras .ij. fois ou .iij.,	And bind and join it, and have the herbs higher than where you're healing, and rub the arm two or three times.
puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans;	Then slightly loosen the bandage above in the middle, for when it's too tight or not enough, then it can't heal properly;
et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on;	And then rub the area with hands until the veins swell up, and one can feel them;
puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier,	Then moisten the flame of a small amount of old oil, then place your left hand's finger on that vein right below the shoulder slightly or where one wants to cauterize;
que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	so that the vein does not burn and rupture upon being pricked.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit,	For there are veins that behave like strings when cauterized, and some have such a strong suction force.
si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus;	If one places it over the flame, it withdraws to the flame, and cannot open the way, and thus belongs to those;
et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	And if it opens the way, then the wound is too narrow, for this reason it means that the surgeons should be experienced in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein starts working for the first time, that's good; if not, it can still be attempted again a little around the same spot or suddenly, provided that the limb is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse .i. jor ou .ij., et ne liier mie le bras:	And if the limb is swollen and the patient feels pain, it should be left for one or two days, without tying up the arm:
par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait;	By chance there will come pus filled blisters; do not enter or bathe, then restart the cleaning if it pleases her;
et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement;	and if the duct is small, or if the tube opening is delicate and you doubt that blood is not escaping as much as you see, if firmly in that same duct straight to all the flame directly;
et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	and let the operation proceed somewhat quickly, so that the limb swells; for this has happened many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile;	If you see the limb swelling, do not restart the cleaning again, and place a little oil on it instead, for it relieves the body of the pain from blood and heals the wound where the oil is placed.
et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc;	And so administer oil to each wound you heal, for it stops the flow of blood;
et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	And similarly perform treacle and bone setting when you place them on the head; if the skin is too tight or slippery due to its thickness.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite,	And if it comes to large abscesses that occur often, even when it has not been healed before because at that time the opening of the vein is small,
si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre;	If you rush, place a wet sponge on the head in warm water and some wine, and hold it for an hour;
et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie;	And it is necessary for you to do this after the blood has left the vein, and if it remains in its place after several days without any sign of blackness or greenness, or does not harm it;
et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if you see this, apply some aloes or myrrh dissolved in the juice of calamus, amber, or something similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times an abscess would develop and show signs in the area of healing: therefore put your hand there, and if you find that part soft under the pressure of your hand, then this indicates an unhealthy condition.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, do not apply any of the things we have said, for by chance they might damage an artery; but make it once again with dry plaster to harden the area, then treat it with another treatment until it heals.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each person with blood according to the quantity of its virtue and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	And if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see it large, let it remain until it becomes refined; and if it's too hot, let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges;	And it is necessary for the one who is full and fasting, needing blood extraction, that you make him larger incisions, and have the flames wide;
et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant;	And for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and make him healthier with small cuts, often, and you must make him healthier by cutting across, not straight;
et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And this method of healing prevents blood loss and nerve entrapment, and is worth more than the long-term health.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc .iij. fois ou .iiij.	And for the person whose body requires treatment, it is necessary to give them a mixture of meat broth and juice from rhubarb apples; if they are heated, they should be treated with a bleeding ritual three or four times.
Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant. et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And make use of the other things we have said in the section or chapter about fainting, for the evacuation of veins.

And if he wishes to sweat his arm and cleanse it again, if necessary, when he is weakened by much cleansing, he should cleanse gradually, according to the amount of its strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if someone wants to sweat their arm after the first cleansing and they have strong veins, then they should cleanse seven hours after the first cleansing, or after the new hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if one wants to cleanse another part, then one should cleanse on the second day or on the third.

puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson,	Then when you have fulfilled all the conditions of health, and place your hand on his heart when it is healthy, so that death does not occur instead of healing.
et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens;	And this happens many times, when the healers are neglectful;
et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus;	And it is not right when you see a limb escaping and blood coming out the second time, and the constriction has closed, that you press forcefully;
ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz;	If it's a shoulder dislocation, do not extend the arm quickly; for this would cause harm.

et met sus .i. poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	and place one part of salt dissolved in water, and gently press it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it alone without compressing it until the abscess subsides.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if you need to bleed again from the blood, should it be healthy in that place itself, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein is healthy in the place of the main vein because it is made up there.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges;	And the method of healing involves bathing their hand in hot water until the veins become red;
puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc;	Then bind it moderately, so that you can see the vein clearly, then now heal through it, neither wide nor long;
et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez;	And if the cuts are wide, and if you have them very close to the joint of the hand, and if there is no way for it to come out, then place the hand in hot water, and let blood flow in the water, as long as you need.
et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit;	And if it's frostbite, do not put the hand in hot water, because you would make it worse in winter than frostbite.
et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And this vein is more healed compared to all other veins; there are no arteries or nerves in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere:	The healing of the salvation of the right hand is equivalent to all diseases concerning the liver, and this is the method:

et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	and then immerse the hand in hot water, if it is frozen at the wound site, and cannot escape.

And when you have treated for the blood as much as your skill allows, place on the vein, oil and wax to quickly fuse together, and thus proceed with each patient.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The cure for one in the left hand corresponds to the disease of the mouse; and do exactly as I have instructed you regarding the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors,	The remedy for the sore throat is effective against all diseases that are in or on the body,
si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	such as gynecological diseases, congestion of flowers (possible medical term for bloating or swelling), diseases of the kidneys, and leg ailments, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere,	And concerning their health, it is that patients bathe in hot water, and rub the vein until it dissolves,
et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains;	And above the ankle joint; and the vein is at the ankle, and upward from the ankle goes in many directions.
saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	So the sound or larger veins, whether at the ankle or at the ankle itself, are those that move.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it at the ankle, beware of the nerves that are nearby, and heal from there as when cooking; and let the fire be in front.

Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz;	And if it is salt from the first time, if you repeat the second one slightly above, because the veins are salty;
ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	Nor should you doubt about the nerve, as we have said before, and do likewise on the other side.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The thigh muscle of the sciatic vein is at the ankle on the back side, and its inflammation corresponds to pain in the buttocks when it's due to hot blood.

car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant;	For otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, you should heal in all possible ways, and also across;

Des sainies de ventouse	Poultices made from suckering
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Blunt suction cups are made from horns, or spiders, or leeches; and suction therapy is performed in two ways: by piercing to draw blood or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu;	And this suction method that involves piercing can be done in two ways: either hot or not using heat;
et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en .xiiij. leus dou cors,	And ventilation, which is done through piercing and extraction of blood, is performed with twelve strokes on each side of the body,
de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col;	Of these, one is entirely in the sun's rays; and the other is exposed to the neck;
et .ij. autres en .ij. costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton;	And two of them on each side of the neck; and the suction cup under the chin;
et li ventouse des .ij. espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies;	And the suction cup at both shoulders; and the suction cup over the knees;
et les ventouses emmi les .ij. bras; et les ventouses des .ij. jambes;	And suction cups on both arms; and suction cups on both legs;
et les ventouses des .ij. chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char,	and suction cups at the ankles; and suction cup treatment does not target blood, for it is present in small veins that are scattered throughout the flesh,
et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne;	and because of this, one does not weaken oneself at all, as one would do with bloodletting;
et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	and it should not be administered at any time, nor in the heat of fire or with sense of fire, in any disease that comes from overabundance, until all parts are emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens;	And if suction is necessary for diseases or out of habit, we should perform it each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between and at each time;
car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief;	for there are some who, when they need to suction, weigh first;
et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz;	and for those who find congestion and redness in their face, and on their head, and at the neck, and darkness in their eyes;
et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc;	and for those who find a drop of blood in their mouth, have swollen tongues, and cough up blood.
et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if there are those who think, and see by means of blood, wounds, and suchlike things.

Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors;	The health of the womb helps in the healing of the head sickness... which comes from the eyes, and it's not right for this to happen after the expulsion of everything from the body;
et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique,	And this suction is part of the treatment of head health,
et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement;	And it is not suitable for those with cold constitution to use, or who have fever, for this causes great harm to them;
et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	And because of this, it is not suitable for those using ice baths, or those who suffer from cold illnesses.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And the one who often bathes in it, becomes oblivious, and because of this, you should place the suction cup slightly further down due to the risk of becoming oblivious.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis,	Suction at the neck is in the place of cold bathing and basilica, for this reason it is effective for tightening the heel.
et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion;	And to cut through the channel of the heart, and suddenly, and to refill;
et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And it should be lightly squeezed, for if it is held too tightly, it may cause obstruction of the lungs or stomach and heart.

And it is in the location of the health of the basilica; and you should instruct the surgeon to hold his hand when placing it, not to grasp the artery, and not to allow repeated bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The ventilation over the chin is associated with illness in the mouth and gum decay, as well as similar diseases that occur within the mouth; it involves the health of both lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation over the shoulders is associated with illness that comes from heat and congestion.

Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The suction cup on the shoulder is useful for hemorrhages from beneath and various diseases nearby. It should be large and made of animal hide since it needs to be well treated. By chance, if it were too fine, it might break and cause significant injuries.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Leg suction cups need to be applied directly as they draw blood from the entire body, and they are beneficial for old pains in the kidneys, bladder, and urethra, and they alleviate swellings; they are placed at the knees, ankles, and sometimes they weaken the body after long use, causing emaciation in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the suction cup is as follows: place it initially while empty, apply a steady suction, quickly apply it, move it evenly, and keep doing this until you see the skin turn red and swell up. Then stop when you perceive the reddish hue due to blood; afterwards remove the suction cups, and take care of your body placement since some individuals have thin flesh with clear pores: one must pierce once only in such cases, make cuts wide but not too deep, and apply gentle suction.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the artery is large, it's necessary to make two cuts: the first time to delicately clear the path of the large blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the artery is very thick, it's necessary to make a third cut; and when we wish to drain little by little from the blood, it suffices to do it only once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement,	And if we wish to remove much blood, we often proceed this way; and if the artery is thick, we pierce it completely, and the ends are such that the veins are pierced suddenly.
et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif:	And it is necessary for the one who has thick skin and hardness, and has contracted sores, that you grease their limbs with suction cups where an opening appears and a dissolving agent:
se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite;	If it's in the state of being purple oil, or sweet almond oil, or pumpkin seed oil;

et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And it should be known when he needs to be suctioned and when he has been suctioned.

et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And it is wise to take the lungs, but it should not be that which is hot drinks.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz,	The suction cups that are placed to irritate are those that are placed on the liver, and on the kidneys, and in gout, and on the belly and the uterus and the bladder, and in the hip, because this member does not endure being irritated by suction on wounds.
