et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu;	And relieve the pain when there is an obstruction or stone, so it relieves the pain by its attractive power in case of obstruction, or empties the stone from its place;
et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue,	And thus she does when you put her on the liver and the lungs if there is retained suction,
et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede,	And these cups are used empty to suck only; and never are used together with fire, and they are not filled with water either.
si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	If it's diseases due to crying, and in such a manner can we fill the suction cup with hot water, or with water that has cooked medicinal herbs suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the heated suction cup applied is as follows:
Et ait .ij. dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu .i. petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille,	And it has two and a half inches in width from front to back, and at its center on both sides there is a small sharp point, just like one would use to pierce an awl,
et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre;	And let it be made of horn, smooth on the front so that it does not irritate the patient upon placing it on the limb;
et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise,	And there is midway an inch long across of spider leg or iron, for putting a candle in place.
et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent;	and they be both large and small according to the diseases and age of those who take them;
car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	for the suction cups for children are different from those for adults, and the thin ones are different from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre:	And one should place this suction cup thus on the limb:
empren la chandoile de cire ou .i. linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse,	Take a candle wax plug or one piece of linen, and place it inside the suction cup at the opening of the penis which is within the suction cup,
si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide;	so that the heat is at the bottom of the suction cup and does not burn the testicles;
et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse;	and then place it on the member, and hold your fingers on the same spot that we have said, so when you want to, if the steam goes, remove the suction cup;
et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	and apply the paste in the same way as before, and repeat it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement;	In suction therapy therefore, which is administered in the disease of pleurisy, there should be no stickiness or lack thereof, and it is only used when it is full of water, and placed solely on the limb.
et c’est li forme:	and this is its shape:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus;	Suction methods are not used only for limbs where we cannot place suction cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar areas;
et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans;	and on the underbodies of animals like hooves or noses, and other similar areas.
et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren;	And if you find veins that are clean and free of pus in clear water, take them;
et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres;	and place them in sweet water until they are familiarized and have nothing inside.
et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues;	and then cleanse the limb with bleeding and suction cups, then rub the limb until it turns red, and place the veins on it.
et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	and when they are full and bleed, if there is a place where suction cups can be placed, then do so, as this does not last much.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint;	If not, raise it with ease, then with water, quite well, and then incision;
et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille .i. drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés;	and if the joints swell too much after the course of the arrows, cool it with one and a half linen cloths dipped in cold water, and place them until the arrow wounds are whitened;
et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez;	and if there are multiple arrows, then apply powdered vitriol or garlic and similar substances until they turn white;
ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant;	or you put half of peeled peas on the wound and leave them there until they dry out on the wound, which will now stop bleeding;
et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	And if you need more skill, take other assistants.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse,	And if the assistants are not willing to help, then rub with fresh blood, or you stick an awl in until the blood comes out.
et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent;	Then place them, and as soon as they feel the blood, they should strengthen;
et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And when you see that they are bleeding, powder a little aloes and finely ground wheat or ash on them; they will now improve.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book of fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is many times necessary in the art of medicine, and restoration of fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent;	Know this, dear boy, that the leaves of this chapter, they contain nothing that was ever found in any old books, nor did anyone read a letter from it;
et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin;	And for this reason, the knowledge has been lost in our land, because I have never found anyone skilled in it;
et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie;	And I know nothing of this, having studied the ancient books by which I have treated that science so much through knowledge and experience, as well as practical experimentation, and through my daily routine;
et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces .ij. chapistres ci devant.	And I have described in this chapter what is contained here, abbreviated it at the end, and clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, just as I did in the previous two chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	So it is necessary that we outline or introduce the main points of this book in its preface and chapters where the senses engage understanding, and remain truthful, so that those who have experienced it may know and learn this noble craft, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars;	I say that when dislocation or fracture or twists or bruises occur to any part of the body, it is necessary for you to quickly treat the patient on both sides, without missing anything, such as weakness due to age, children, or elderly individuals;
ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	If the cautery is not too tight, or too cold; and consume cool foods, which means cold meats, and liver and rabbit meat, and do not drink wine, nor consume any fatty meats, and do not fill yourself with too much meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have doubts about an abscess infection, nor spreading of material in the limb; if the patient feels well under their initial regime they've been using.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that you consume meats which cause heavy digestion or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and leeks, and kidneys, and pies, and beef spleens, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar items.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For this kind of digestion causes motion and more quickly the breaking (or disruption) is resolved.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans;	Know that when bones break in old and aged individuals, they cannot be healed or joined properly according to their natural state due to the withering of limbs. Also, for those who are too tender, such as bones of young children;
mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet .i. gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	But do not worry about it, reset the broken bone. For large protruding bones that separate and unite the limb together again, until it can withstand as before; and do not allow any movement in his work, for this requires feeding him with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	Know that fractures occur in various ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the foot, or leg, and in this chapter I will tell you all the ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go to the arm, and others when sharpening, such as sawing through a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And in case of breakage with wound, and breakage resulting from a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu;	And for each way it has its own instrument, and its proper tool in the restoration process, according to whatever memory comes to mind;
et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main;	and is known by the breakage of the bone when the limb is twisted and opens well outward, and hurts under the pressure of the hand;
et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure;	And when there is no twisting or misalignment of the limb at the socket, and if the patient does not feel significant pain in the body part, should there be no breaking;
mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	but it may well have a twist or crack, or a small break.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not suitable for you to move it by hand, but apply the following remedies, and then gently correct it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les .ij. parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne;	And know that the break that occurs internally, and with the two parts being disjointed, you should now put them in an equal position, so that abscesses are placed one above the other;
et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez;	And if pus forms and comes, if he lets it go for any day, until the pus becomes calm;
puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	Then place it evenly with what you can do lightly and wisely, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than when there are pieces. Then tighten him, as it should be done according to this.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de .ij. pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a .ij. cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main;	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, if it is separated by two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or at your hand if it's a small limb, or by two strings, or by one string and at your hand;
et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor;	and place the limb according to its natural form, so that when the parts of the broken member are removed, then adjust it in all directions by your means at their usual position where you can, and guard that through your work no injury or pain befalls the patient;
et ajoste bien les .ij. chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And adjust well the two joints of bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if you think it is not quite right: do it beautifully in position, don't pull too much, and apply pressure as those who bring about discharge through a wound and muscle contraction do to the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere;	And when the limb is in place, chastise well the patient so they do not move it, whether awake or asleep, turning or in any other manner;
et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And make sure that the limb is securely set so that the person does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor;	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet at the correct spot, and it must be placed in such a position that he does not feel any pain;
et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez;	and make sure it is placed straightly, so there is no twisting when it is restored;
et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	and the quality of the broken limb should be according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken limbs are various in size and degree, and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz;	For there are small limbs, such as arms and legs and similar: it is necessary to envelop them with soft and fine linen cloths;
et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche;	And those that are larger, such as thighs and legs: it is necessary to envelop them with wide, hard ropes, for wide ropes encompass the entire large limb, restraining it equally from all sides, so that there is no twist;
puis lie entor estoupes legieres, .iij. tours ou iiij. selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure;	Then tie them loosely around with lighter bands, 3 or 4 according to the limb's size, and hold your hand a little on the rope as you go around it, then proceed above the joint and restrain less, so that the joint can move slightly away from its position;
et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren .i. autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet;	And gradually make the band softer and softer, until you have treated most of the healthy part, then take another band, and go around again from above the joint;
puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus;	Then return to the part below the fracture, and apply pressure moderately, neither too strongly nor too weakly, as we have said in the first lesson above;
puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus .i. bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Then place between the heated threads of linen or cloth until they are all equal, then tie everything above with one band, and then put your well-made stars on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors;	And if there's a swelling or an abscess, place something soothing on it that removes the swelling and leaves it in such a state for some days;
puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	Then apply pressure to the stars, and make them half as wide as a thick stick, or from the wood used for making staffs, or from palm tree leaves, and they should be arranged like this:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres;	However, it is necessary that the iron rod which one places on the fracture should be a bit larger and wider than the others;
et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor;	and also as long as it is appropriate to the size of the limb whether small or large.
puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure;	then hold it on the rods in the same way that you did in the first attempt, then tie an additional strap over it, just like you tied in the first attempt over the fracture;
plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol;	tightly fasten this more than before, but not too much; it is necessary that the thread be of medium thickness, neither too thick nor too thin, and should be made of soft linen;
car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	For if the threads are thick, as in works made by humans who weave their linen cords twisted, and this is a great mistake, because the thread cannot be equal if it's too fine, and it doesn't suit for there to be less than half a finger's width between each row.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patients are injured by the rings after tightening them on their healthy parts, then put linen or woolen bandages over them, so they don't blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is swollen and the joints are broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not proper to strain all broken limbs on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés .v. jors ou .vij., ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant;	For when the limbs are large, it is not proper to apply pins straightaway but rather after five days or seven, or more depending on your judgment each time an abscess appears;
et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	And here is the method of the old plastering for restoring fractures, dislocations, and twists: take some flour that sticks to the mill walls, mix it with plenty of egg, and make this concoction neither too thin nor too thick. Use this application, and this is the common method of restoring fractures in various positions, as well as for women and small children, because it is not too expensive or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering for restoring fractures and dislocations and twists: take three parts of each of these ingredients - garlic, dill, rue, and asafetida - mixed with three times the weight in powdered gum arabic and myrrh; add five parts aloes. Grind all together into a fine powder and mix it with plenty of egg; if the mixture is warm, use this plaster, for it has a good composition and rapidly heals broken bones, and it is beneficial to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .viiij. З.; acaice vi. З.; bolic armenic .x. З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering for dislocation: take mugwort and myrrh, in quantity of 3 parts; frankincense and aloes, in quantity of 8 parts; meadowsweet vi parts; Armenian balm in 10 parts, grind well together, mix with vinegar or sufficient egg white, and apply.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu. Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Another method of plastering for joints and bones cut open, to alleviate the pain caused and tenderness, and for bone cutting: take new wool and its grease cooked in oil, put it on your wound. These plasters do not heal completely but are better for soothing abscess fever and properly treating bone pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plastering that heals broken bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial oak leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme. Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Another method for setting a broken bone and removing pus. Take roots of valerian, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of ginger, one part each; grind them, mix with wine, and if the limb is warm, mix it with moist coriander water, or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre. Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Another way of plastering more strongly than the first when pus is in the process of restoring the limb. Take valerian roots, and linseed seeds, borage, clover, and watercress, as well as violet and chamomile flowers, one part each; grind them, mix with saltwater, or sweetened water, or wine according to the heat of the limb and its rest period.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ispocrates says that for restoring strength to a broken limb, only balm made of beeswax and oil should be applied, and no other thing besides. He states that it should be soft enough between two fingers without being too sticky or too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen that we should apply to the broken limb for restoration, things dried but slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloes and incense and similar things, just as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to plaster for injury and pain: take mussels and offals from slaughtered animals, or bird feathers, and vervain, and milk of equal measure. Crush them, make a paste, and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors	And then remove a little later, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is his bone in its place injured; if not, remove it by hand.
Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor;	And if pain comes to the limb, or itching, that causes no rest or swelling, then hurry and remove it, and apply the plaster now; take light linen and a wet sponge, and dip them in water, and wash the limb until the itching stops and the pain is relieved;
puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut;	Then let the limb rest for an hour, then place it on dry wool, moistened in water or oil of roses, and secure it with a bandage until you are sure there's no pus;
et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let the inflammation rest on the limb, and reduce the pain, then restart the gentle healing process, and add a little plaster, but don't apply it as tightly as before; and proceed gently until it's sound.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that pus and redness, pain, swelling are present throughout the affected area, and you need to apply plaster and bandages, then restart as you did initially, in exactly the same manner.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou .iiij. ou .v. ou .vij.; et aucune fois le laisse .xx. jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus;	And if nothing of what we have said happens to the limb, or if it is not released until after three days, four, five, or seven; and each time leave it for twenty days, according to this method, as long as the healing process continues, and progresses towards reattachment of the tissue.
adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir;	Therefore the healing should go beyond what it was at first, and the body will regain its strength as I have explained before; and if you see that the skin is drying more than necessary, know that no remedies can be applied.
arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure;	Apply hot water regularly each day when you reset the dislocation, and let it be every third day, and gently cleanse the area.
par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	Through this process, correct the dislocation of substances in the limb, and immediately fix what foolish people do, causing the member to be forcibly restored: this is bad. Such actions are dangerous and unnecessary; I can only advise rest and correctly opening it.
des diverses manieres de brisure	through various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees;	Many ways of fractures exist, and various forms, and their causes are distinct;
car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	because there are fractures caused by the impact of a sword, and in these cases, the skull bone crushes all the way to the base of the bone, just below the skull, as if it is breaking the bone; thus this kind of fracture is called "hacking" or "halving".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or when the sword cuts through the bone from above without piercing it, this kind of fracture is called "absolute" or "clean"; and these are either large or small injuries caused by such fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or crack in the bone, or through stone, or on stone, or other similar cases.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture that reaches up to the ligament surrounding the bone, or above the bone, and this injury can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»;	And if there's a wound that penetrates into the bone as finely as a hair, and has small cracks, and because of this it is called this 'hairline' fracture;
et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is made by striking with a stone or falling, or by something similar, and causes part of the bone to break inward, and has its fragments as close together as candle holders when they are fitting into the candles; if it penetrates the stone from within.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant;	This happens more in those with wet bones beneath, such as children's bones;
et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are various methods of breaking up substances where small pieces are removed such as these; and I will discuss them in their proper place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all methods of breaking through by taking away from them, and the examination of attempts, and by the putrid matter which is upon.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair appearance is known when one has exposed the bone and rubs it inside, for then you open the black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In treating the breakage, beware of the bad occurrences due to the malady, and if you see no harmful accident such as vomiting bile, loss of appetite, stretching, dizziness, fever, or other symptoms in various conditions, then there is no certainty for recovery.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see an alarming accident and hope for salvation, then start the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the knuckle first comes to you, and it's in winter, then you should remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the start of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in summer, then hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh around the bone becomes rotten, and accidents occur as we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues,	And if the bone fracture reaches the membrane that covers the brain, then you should split the fractured part like this: and take hold of the head from the diseased limb, and expose it on the bone in all ways that you can, and according to the shape of the wound as much as you can.
et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset;	And when the flow of blood comes to reveal the bone, or if pus is present, you should assist with what's necessary, and it is that you fill the wound with moist cloths soaked in rose oil;
et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc .ij. manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And have the wound rest until the pus has calmed and there is assurance of blood flow; then begin working toward the bone to extract it, and this can be done in two ways: one way is that you cut with a narrow incision upfront, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another incision larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is that you have several sizes of incisions, some narrow and others broad, all with points, made from metal and work them gently, making sure not to injure the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is out and hard, it is necessary that you pierce inside it, in such a way that you apply cuts with needles, not completely but so that they do not penetrate beyond the bone at all times; and there should be an opening or circumference of about 1 inch above the point where no part of the needle can pass through the bone. And you must have more than one, so that each goes into its place of the thickness of the bone, in such a way that you have needles for all sides; and this is the form of three types of needles:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing through the broken bone is that you place one needle on the bone and turn with your hands until you know that the bone has been pierced. Then move the needle elsewhere a little after, and do this throughout; then cut along the incisors of the gap between the bones where they are apart, and do it more finely than possible and gently, as we have said, until you can pull the bone to your hand or any tool you have like forceps, and be sure not to touch the brain or spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout .i. autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire;	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, it is necessary that you finish smoothing out what remains of the gap between bones with another tool similar to an incisor but it should be stronger and more delicate than the other incisors;
et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a .i. des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And if there remains any small bones or no scales at all, gently remove them with instruments of one inch in length; then treat the wound with bandages and remedies that we have described.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of operating is this, as Galen stated, which is safer; and the knife should be quite strong, for it's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	Firstly, you should uncover a portion of the bone, where the fracture opens and moves, so that when you have uncovered that part, you will place under the tip of this lens-shaped incision, as described here.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en .ij. costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz;	And do not cut from one side only, and let that part be in two segments, so that the cutting is toward the bone; then strike with a small hammer above, so you gently crush the entire bone, and take care to keep away any mesh that is nearby.
s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	If it is pressed against bone, gently apply force to it, because the bone is quite sensitive and can cause pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone break does not go all the way through the membrane, and only part of the bone is cut above, with small fragments remaining, it's necessary to clean up any roughness afterwards. Use a thin razor for removing scales that you should have in different quantities, so as to apply the most suitable treatment in each case according to the treatise and the nature of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you're facing large razors and then even finer ones, don't stop doing this until it's done well.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other kind of hair trimming and fine breakage, you must apply the treatment according to its location; this is something that cannot be left to anyone who has devoted their studies to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes .i. drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie;	And if the wound is uncovered, it is necessary for you to take one linen bandage according to the size of the wound, soak it in oil roset and place it on the wound;
puis pren .i. autre drapeil doublé en .ij. ou en .iij., et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus .i. autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement;	Then take another bandage double thickness in two or three layers and soak it in wine and oil roset, then place it on the first bandage; do this as lightly as possible so you don't weigh down the wound, then apply a further layer of strips over it, but don't pull them too tightly so that they only touch the wound.
et le laisse ensi .i. jor ou .ij., tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication;	And keep it like this for one or two days until the abscess is no longer inflamed, then release it and apply medications such as wildflower roots, flour of camphor, incense powder, and similar substances; and from these things make a powder, apply it to the wound, and give further medicated remedies without causing irritation.
et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And make sure the wound is clean immediately, do not leave any pus behind, nor allow any matter to be assembled at all, for when matter assembles upon the skin near the brain, it will flow and proliferate and cause great harm to the patient; for when one places something piercing above this, it becomes corroded from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Then take care, so if no accidents happen to the patient, as we have said, if there is a doubt it should not be doubted.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et .iij. parties d’oile roset et en glue .i. drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac;	And if it happens only because of the medicine that we have put on, and should this virtue be present, then you should take one part of honey and three parts of rose oil and mix them into a paste with one cloth piece, and place it on the affected area;
puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the treatment of various treatments is necessary, as long as he remains healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two nasal parts above or beneath which is broken once, or only one by itself, because they are two bones; and this lower part is cartilaginous, it does not break at all, even if forced or twisted, then it heals.
Et se l’une des .ij. parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil;	And if one of the two parts is broken, it is necessary that you bend your small finger or thumb by the nose, and place an equal break inside on your second finger, and at the base towards the front, until the nose revives according to its natural shape;
et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And do this gently, and beware that the patient does not feel pain through your action.

Et se li brisure est de .ij. pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues;	And if the break is in two parts, redo the procedure, and try to restore on the first day if you can;
se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	But if not, after the seventh or eighth day when the abscess has calmed down, then try to bring back up from the nose head towards the linen cloth bandage, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you should bring up two others from the other side, if the break is there; and make them so large that they fill the hollows of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor. Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	And it is said that one should moisten the tents with butter and change them each day. And in each instance use goose feathers instead of tents, and if you have one egg worth of dressing to cover it completely, then keep the wound clean, letting air pass through; simply do as you see fit.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if abscesses come up to the nose as you work on them, then apply a poultice or wet cotton in oil, or a pinch of lavender oil.

et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is no wound within the bone, then treat it, and apply cloves until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	regarding the rupture of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is fractured and there's no wound at the surface, and only the breakage is outside completely, not broken into two parts but rather split internally within, one can easily identify it.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary; if the breakage is in the right part, you should bend your index finger into the mouth towards the sore area; and if the breakage is in the left jawbone, you should bend your index finger of the right hand instead, and gently press on the breakage internally, and then proceed to the other hand by pushing it outward, and place them evenly.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the breakage of the jawbone extends for two inches, then it is necessary that you apply an extension of two inches until they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the movements of the teeth occur, or rupture, then you should restrain them with a thread of gold or silver or silk. Then place on the broken mandible plaster, and place on one piece two folded cloths; and place on that cloth a large flag made well, or a piece of leather equal in size to the mandible, and stick it on as best you can, and command the patient to rest, and consume light meats.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you notice that the figure changes, or that it loosens by the third day, and then set back what has changed; and apply plaster, mixing with powder from the mill with plenty of eggs or flour of yolk, after you have removed the plaster; and place on the plaster light wool, and if the plaster hardens, and the patient's condition does not change, let it be until they are healed. Many times heal in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if abscesses appear, then apply what we have instructed many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a breakage and wound together, reward any piece of the bone that has been removed; so much skill is required for the extraction tools suitable for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with fire according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, if it is large, cover the wound with one dressing suitable for this purpose to promote healing until it is healed.
de la forcele	by strength
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The force breaks many times before reaching the shoulder, and the break occurs in three ways: when it is broken and removed cleanly with two parts, and there are pieces left, making it easier to restore; or when there's a break accompanied by an injury.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the veins are such that when there is a break accompanied by an injury, you have two assistants, so that one feels for the shoulder where force has broken; and the other extends to the neck towards the affected part. And if you cannot draw the head from the strength at the back due to it coming in front, then it is necessary for the patient to lie on their shoulder blade and put half an armpit under them, and push the shoulder down until the bone of the strength lifts.

et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit. de la brisure de l’espaule	Of the breaking of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus .i. drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en .xx. jors ou en xxv,  Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Sometimes the shoulder breaks or dislocates either at its ends or in the middle, and it often happens due to a hit; you should adjust according to the shape of the breakage and reset accordingly with their natural form. Do this in all possible ways you can. Then sprinkle the shoulder with ground from the mill mixed with plenty of eggs, apply light compresses, and place two cloths on top. Next, place a large, subtle wedge slightly wider than the shoulder, ensuring that there are no gaps under any part of the shoulder; fill the gap with strips of linen to ensure the wedge fits evenly. Then tighten it into one big bend firmly so that the wedge doesn't move from its place and watch each day; whenever it loosens, tighten again making sure the wedge is in line if it is out of place, lay the patient on their side; and the shoulder will be fixed back in place after 20 days or 25. And when this number is completed, remove the dislocation, you can be certain because it isn't bone that easily fits together.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut. de la brisure de l’ajutoire	regarding the breaking of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The assistants are those that are between the blade and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, you must restore it according to one of these two methods: of which one is that you take a solid stick of medium thickness, according to this shape:

And tie two pieces of cloth together, and bend them up, then place the patient's broken arm on top of one seat; then pour the broken part over the stick until it reaches the elbow, and has made half a turn with the length of the stick, then bend over any heavy object or let assistants hold it downwards; then put the pieces of cloth so that the break is evenly between their hands, until the broken part returns as it should.

And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, hold one band over the cut and another above it, spreading each minister to their part.
