Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns .iij. jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois. Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you see the base of the stakes and their constriction, as we have said, in the hour when you restore the broken limb, and if you doubt about discharging pus, if you let it be bound until a week's time, as we have said; then observe each three days' bond, to ensure that itch does not swell or come near to the body, or that ulcers cannot reach the limb because they are too narrow. If there is an issue, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés .iij. jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire .i. cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse. Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en .xl. jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.  Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier .l. jors ou .ij. mois.	And if no such incidents occur, or if the loosening is only done after two days or more, and keeps lying in bed on his back, with his hands on his stomach; and place under him one cloth filled with equal wool for support, and observe each hour of the day that the figure of the broken limb does not move, or that the bonds do not soften; if it heals through the power of medicine, and he gives meat as we have placed before, in such a manner that the meat is at the first subtle; and when it begins to recover, if it becomes large. And custom dictates that both the brace and the leg should be recovered within forty days altogether; then you must loosen and apply baths and medicines for the body to heal properly.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is made of two bones which are called the 'foscile' pair. One bone is small and it forms the socket; the other is larger and it is beneath the small one towards the back of the hand. By chance, only the large foscile might break, or just the smaller one, or perhaps they both break together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	When only the small fosciles break, the restorations are light and the healings; but when the large ones break, the healing is ill and more painful than if they broke together. If it's just the small foscile that breaks, then a slight extension should be appropriate and setting them evenly is required.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus .i. cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et .i. cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a .i. liien, et uns autres ministres a .i. autre au desus. Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And if it's the large foscile that breaks, you should hold them tighter; then extend on one cushion and pinch the hand socket higher than the others, and position the small bones lower than the other ones. Make sure the muscles are crossed over themselves, with an additional cushion in front positioned higher so that they don't endure any strain; next, extend your arms' tendons towards their joint above their hands or at one elbow, and another attendant should do the same on the opposite side. Then place them evenly according to their best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breakage into pieces, you place each back in its position, and if there is none of them that grabs the knee, and you cannot restore it to its place, then cut through and the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if in case of injury during surgery, I mentioned this earlier in detail; take care of the treatment.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue .i. drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie .i. drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez. Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir vj. esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en .ij.; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit. Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And if during the beginning of the restoration, there occur pus pockets, then apply: take a strip made from rosin and white beeswax that is neither too hard nor too soft; and attach this strip so finely that it covers the pus pockets until they subside. And then remove the wax, and place the plaster powder mixed with an egg, and set the splints, ensuring the splint on the injury site is more firmly placed than others, slightly wider than the rest, and remember to have seven or eight splints in various positions: if the injury affects one bone, two bones; and place it more above the injury area compared to other parts; and each day remove from that point further outward, as I mentioned at the start of this chapter; ensure that the strips covering the injury are soft and moist, not hard or abrasive; and use threads made of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have stated. And take care of the limb and the joint after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer. Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And if any bad incidents occur to the limb, such as itchiness that comes to the limb, it is necessary for you to soak the limb in hot water until that itchiness is relieved; and let the limb not be allowed to rest. And then resume compression, and if the ligaments have been severed and the bone exposed, along with similar things, if you can, address this issue accordingly.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if precautions are taken so that no injuries can come to the limb because it is too tight, it is necessary for you to soften it with oil, and leave it like this for a few days, until the pains subside, and then resume compressing it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a .xx. jors. ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en .xxx. jors ou en .xxxv., et par aventure en .xx. jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	And if none of these things that we have mentioned do come to the patient, nor does it need to be released up until twenty days or more. Or wherever else, then allow them to use their hands on their neck, and ensure their necks are equal, and take care to avoid movement and stretching, and sleep on their back; and know that this strain has been healed for thirty days or thirty-five days, and perhaps in twenty days, according to the compositions and the characteristics of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	On the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	You should know that on the back of the hand and in our fingers, there are few breaks, and they only occur multiple times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the heel of the hand or finger is broken or sprained, it should be treated by applying splinting, keeping the hand straight in front of them as well; then place their hand on an extended surface and extend the fractured bones, putting them even with each other until they are properly aligned; and put a plaster and bandages if there's no pus discharge, then apply a pillow according to the size of the wound; and wrap it loosely in one linen sheet.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the breakage is in between the toes near the belly of the foot's sole, then make a strip of cloth and instruct the patient to apply it to their broken toe; and then wrap it tightly with a long piece of cloth, and place the pillow so that its width matches the size of the hand's palm, and secure it properly.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is at the front, it should be that you place an elevation above and another below in the heel, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind them all together with the hand, and seal the connection between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break occurs at neither of our fingers, if it is in the joint, as is fitting; and bind with the heel, and if you see, place a small upright stick to raise the break, and don't move it; and if the break is on other fingers, like in the index or one of the others, place them equally, and bind with the healthy finger that comes after; or bind all together holding tightly, so nothing moves, or place a stick as you would hold; take care in the restoration and positioning of each wound, and deal with whoever brings it to you, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bone of the elbow is often broken, and one can see this when it turns in front and behind; and the restoration involves binding over the breakage .i., above the fracture, and .i., another underneath.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the injuries lie on her face, then extend each minister his link to his equal part; and this is when the breakage enters the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure. Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses .ij. mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if the breakage is near the base of the arm, then one should place his links towards the wrist, and the other links over the breakage. Similarly, if it's near the elbow, then you should place the links behind the elbow, and the extension downwards; then put the sights on the bone equally to his two hands, as long as it follows its natural shape, and then apply the plaster, and the link, if there's no abscess.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess around it, let it heal first before returning to your work and treatment; the healing process is carried out in this manner.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure .i. bendeil dur doublé en .ij. ou .iij., et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute .i. fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment .iij. tors ou iiij. sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as .ij. chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie .iij. esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the wound, i.e., bandage it with three or four layers of thick material, and retain excess length. Then raise the leg until the heel reaches the root of the thigh, and insert a thread one meter long between the calf and leg, downwards from the knee to just below it. Then guide the ends of the thread upwards through loops at the top; then wrap around the leg and the calf with the bandage, then place an anchor on the wound edge and another under the bone in the leg; then fill the eight inches between the leg and calf with wet cloth strips for equal pressure application, then start to bind tightly in three or four rounds around the wound. And as you go beyond the wound area, bind less tight; then secure two ends of the thread that you've placed between the leg and calf at this point, tie them together with three loops above them, then return under the thread loop until you're below the ankle bone; tighten it so it doesn't move from its place, then leave it like this, then there's no danger of an abscess forming or swelling or any other symptoms.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if such a thing occurs, reposition it and guide the treatment according to what we've said many times; and should there be pieces of bone that are caught, cut them out if possible; and if not, you must cut into the wound and extract the force; then treat as we have instructed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the flesh broken when these needles are inserted like in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, no discomfort arises with the patient during this treatment.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	Know that the flesh is restored within one day, or somewhat less, or somewhat more, depending on the variety of constitutions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	from the alley of the kidney
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois. Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou .i. pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	Know that in the alley of the kidney there is little cracking, but it bends many times. And if it does crack, it's usually just a crack or two parts lost, and this happens to all injuries, whether visible or not, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one should place equal what is round at its ends, until everything can move together. Then put plaster on it, and you can put a round stick if necessary, and then tighten as needed. Then redo all the preparations we've spoken about in other fractures, whether it's discharging pus or any similar situation; for each incident, use what suits that specific case, until everything is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the breaking of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait .ij. os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i.	You know that in the leg there are two bones. One is called 'right' or 'mustelz', and the other is named 'foscile'; and every sort of injury occurs just like it does with the arm, and for this reason, the restoration process is similar to that of the arm and everything proceeds equally.
Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	And if both bones are broken together, twist the leg from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the delicate bones are broken, twist them in front.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz. Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And if the larger bones are broken, one feels great pain and sees it clearly; twist them downwards. Therefore administer extension, and make them equal, binding them evenly; but when the break is irregular or there are multiple pieces, then extension should be more limited and lighter; and align according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your task, take two ropes of wood that strengthen the leg on both sides and should be as long as the leg from the knee down to downwards; then wrap these in two layers each side, binding them up and down and also in the middle, and ensure that the leg cannot decline either right or left. It will be well done this way; and no one administers a plaster as long as it is made of wood and placed on the leg to prevent movement. And do this carefully at the break where there is injury; and move the leg each day to see if there are any abscesses or other complications; treat until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	From bone fractures due to impact
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle it does not come from fracture but from bone impact; there is no once-only fracture and the bones can be displaced. There is only strength depending on multiple positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there occurs a fracture in the bone impact and you see these bones rise over each other, lay the injured bones on the ground like they want to move away. Also do this when the patient is lying down; then press them as much as it takes until their senses return; then apply plaster and bandages on top of that. Place a small table under his feet about half a foot high, then press him onto the floor up to the ankle bend, then wrap cloths around it, and do other things you need to do.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three or four days have passed, if the bandage is removed, because you will find the bones level, whether they are broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there are any of the two broken, repair them, as we said about the fingers of the hand; then place a stick over each broken finger according to their length, and make it slightly wider than that, then put under the foot that board I have mentioned, and tighten the addition against this; and if there are two or three or more, break them, so place on each finger a stick according to its quantity, wrapped in one layer of linen, and tighten the table under this. And stay seated at the top of the table facing the stomach under this, so that it touches well.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you should not forget the other things I've said about other injuries, as we have discussed; and treat each incident according to how it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	regarding the breaking of the bone in the hand
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com .i. sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice .vij. jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of her nature is broken, if it causes enlargement, then let her sit and enlarge further. Then incline her towards the back part, being held from behind; fill the cavity that was natural with cotton, also filling it as large as a finger would be; then lay her down again, lift up her back little by little, and then jump out the cotton until it reaches the entrance of nature and return the bone together with the finger; and when she wishes to urinate, remove the cotton. When she has urinated, get her back and do this for seven days or a bit more: if the break will heal, take a bladder of goats' stomachs, tie a stick at its neck and fill the whole bladder into nature; then blow through the stick until the bladder is inflated internally: nature will return to restore the break. Then fill with cotton and leave like this for some days, until it becomes healthy.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre. Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	And when the bone of the wrist or hand is broken, or in a man, if you restore it as we have said for the hipbone; and do not omit these fractures near him who puts his study and practice to use, and listen to my book. For the break signifies more than various positions of the right way of restoration: therefore understand this.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the case of the penis, if it is broken, take a goose’s throat and fill the penis with it; then wrap it in linen or cloth, and let it be for three days or as long as necessary, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	Regarding breaking with injury
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a break with an injury, even if it's large, like in the case of the shin bone or shoulder blade or any similar injuries, that they should be treated now. The procedures we have mentioned shall attest to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is healed, you can reapply vitriol to it. If there's no other option, then continue with restoring the break in that same hour or day, or even on the same day, provided that abscesses are not coming out.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if there are abscesses coming out, leave the restoration until the next day, as long as the abscess has subsided. Don't touch it on the third or fourth day either, for you might bring about bad accidents by doing so.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the bone breaks and is visible above the uncovered knee, it is necessary for you to place it gently with your hands at a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not visible for you to place evenly with your hands, then use this iron tool made of iron that is .vij. or .viij. long inches, and its width should match the size of the wound; for each breakage treatment, it's necessary for the surgeon to hold about .iii. or iiij., depending on what suits him in each injury case; it should be round with a slight thickness so that it doesn't bend under compression on your limb during the work; and may be sharp at both ends, and thick towards the middle ahead.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre. Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And it is called "palainche" because the crooked ends should be placed on the visible part of the bone; and you hit them once, until they return, making sure they are even against each other. And if the breakage is thin, and the tools cannot properly grasp the bone, then you have to hold the tip of the bone until the tools can take it effectively.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot return the bone back, as we have said, if you have access to an appropriate tool for this task, such as a surgical blade or a small saw, with your strength; then remove what is remaining in the bone through hardness and small cuts.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil. Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille .i. drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	And when the bone is returned and the patient feels intense pain afterwards, know that it has not been placed naturally in its position. Do as you can to place it there, then apply a layer of one part of black vitriol for every three parts of wine, and properly if it's in an erect state; and do not place wax or any other substance where there is pus, so as to prevent the development of gangrene or corruption; then administer these remedies when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound open, and cover it completely according to the size of the wound, and be very cautious that the wound is not strained by bruising; and many times people have done this incorrectly, causing injury or corrosion on the patient's part; and let the compresses be softer and more forgiving than other injuries.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie. Et quant tu vois aprés .i. jor ou .ij. enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And if the wound is deep or large, and you suspect that unwanted complications might occur, as we have said before, and you feel pain in your extremity, it would not be appropriate to apply remedies; but instead cover completely without using compresses. And when after one day or two days you see that the swelling begins to go down at the wound, remove what you had placed with all wine, and apply a healing ointment for wounds, like an ointment from Tetrafarmacon and similar ones.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary for you to dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and at vespers, until it has healed and become healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be put together so that the joint moves easily forward.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if the joints continue to do this for days and it cannot be sewn but remains like that with the joint, know that there are small bone fragments causing this issue. Therefore, you need to work on the wound with a tented method, and remove all these pieces of bone that cause pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant. Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés .xx. jors ou .xxx., puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And if there is an opening at the site or any other form of corruption, it must be treated according to what was instructed in the preceding chapter. And when bone is broken and exposed on the limb, like the bones of the hand or shoulder, or similar large limbs, do not remove them because often this leads to death. However, leave it until it heals; perhaps after 20 days or 30 days, then treat the wound if you can; and if you cannot, just let it be.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The burns that come from sweat
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	The burns often come after rubbing with the breeze, especially near the joints. A terrible thing to see is how the limb's shape changes; and by chance cannot perform its natural actions on it.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then when it is fresh: if you administer stictch medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, sarsagot, carageen, and similar others, do so according to whichever of these you desire or all together, mixing them with stictch wine or with the yolk of an egg or with honey; then apply it on a nut in poultices, bind it well, and don't remove it with your hands for days; afterwards displace it, and start another poultice until the swellings are removed; or you bind onto a well-made piece of cork because the properties of cork are such that they remove all swellings from limbs; if the swelling has turned into hardness like stone and needs to be removed, cover it with a paste, making the excess visible; or take it off with no one's help until it is removed, and treat it until healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	The limb that becomes weak after being garrisoned
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the breakage of the bone is restored, and after that the limbs are weak and subtle, this happens through various causes: because one was tied too tightly, and was not tied as it should have been; or because there were too many ties, and could not bring circulation to the limb; or due to excessive bleeding; or due to large movements not in their time; or because they have little blood in their body, if they are weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the treatment is that you should eat the herb in him, and make the body tender until there are numerous effects within him; then provide baths for him, and give him joy and rest. Afterward, apply ointment to the limb, so that the ointment attracts towards the main circulation, and washes with hot water repeatedly until the circulation matches the limb; and restores his natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	If a limb is bent after recovery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration and the bone is broken apart, though the form of the limb is ugly, it does not lose its natural function: nor should you believe those who say one must break the entire limb anew. And many foolish people have done this in our land; these practices are condemned, causing great harms and even death. However, if the inflammation and torture are still fresh, then it's right to immerse them in hot water, or to cook mollifying herbs such as leaves of basil, roots, and mallow, among similar remedies; and apply one liter of a moistening plaster, such as well-made yarrow extract, and take the basil oil, mix it with tallow or nut oil, and apply the plaster over that. Alternatively, you can take greased figs, grind them with cinnamon powder, and other medicines that soften heat, and then make a plaster from these.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes. Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And always, when treating a dislocation, it is advised to continuously and thoroughly rub the affected area with wet hands. And each hour, allow movement of the limb in its place.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation is old and hardened, like bone, and requires treatment with metal tools, then it might be necessary to operate up to the bone, gently on the delicate incision; and incorporate patience and careful consideration in the healing process.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book on dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, for this reason it cannot move, and the limbs are misaligned, causing patients to experience great pain and severe injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation happens without a cause and if it is about to occur now, you should bring it back without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors;	For if one delays, the limbs swell up and by chance they are put back into place in their original location; because it is not good to move it when it is swollen at that time: it often brings on pus and other pains;
toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	If this happens, if you find the patient in this situation, let the surgeon take care of them until all the pus has subsided; then immerse the limb in warm water and oil, gently move it, and clean each limb as needed based on its place.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have arranged the chapters about the dislocations of the shoulder up to here.
des mandibules	of the jaw
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Sometimes the jaws become dislocated forwards, and the dislocations of both occur in two ways: either they are slightly ossified at their joints and somewhat soft; or they are completely dislocated, hanging towards the chin, causing saliva from the mouth to escape that they cannot contain it, nor can they close their mouth, and wrap their tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it can return through several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie;	And if it's complete and fulfilled, you should reset it quickly without hesitation;
et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de .ij. pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And in such a way that the attendants cut the head with the aid of the surgeon, and push one of his thumbs into the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth; if the dislocation is two inches long; and the other hand should be free to balance; command the patient to soften, his jaws, and move them in every direction.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And push the thumb until it is balanced, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if bringing it back hurts, likewise when the two jaws are together, use hot water and oil, until you gently reset them; do not overly force their return, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens;	And when they are brought back evenly, and the mouth of the patient feels well with mild soothing, then place wet cloths as a poultice made from rose oil and beeswax on it, then bind it lightly with moist strips.
et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre .ij. cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules;	And let the patient rest on their back, and keep their head between two cushions so they do not move to either side nor try to stretch, but please give them light food until the pains are alleviated, and ensure that the jaws are fastened together.
et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And then taste it lightly, and make sure there is no work to opening the mouth for eating or drinking until the jaw is well healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be properly aligned within an hour and are not yet fully restored to their original position, it leads to fevers becoming habituated and recurrent, and in consequence stomach discomfort or even vomiting occurs.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times, death befalls the one who encounters this within eight days.
de la forcelle	from the fortress
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The strength cannot relieve from within the ribcage and the back, and it is relieved once outside, and well can one feel this.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint;	And the restoration is that the patient lies on their back and extends their arms; then press towards your palm with the head and it will return. Then place them on a splint and wrap with a bandage, and support;
et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez;	And the head near the knife cannot be relieved; if not, and if it relieves once, then reset it to its place as we said; then place them on a splint and wrap with a bandage, and support, and instruct the patient to rest until they are healed.
et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And similarly, bring back the shoulder blades when it has been released from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Regarding the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc .iij. manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc;	Know that the shoulder is dislocated only in three ways: out of which one is when it dislocates towards the part of the socket and away from the head; and the second way is at the part below the elbow; and by chance it dislocates upwards, this happens rarely;
et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	And the shoulder never dislocates behind nor within the nerves; and it dislocates from below towards the socket more often, especially in those with little flesh, because they sprain quickly; for those with enough flesh, it jumps to points and returns to them.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance happens to some men from impact or breaking, and the shoulder swells with an acute abscess, and they think it is dislocated due to this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must prove it, as long as you are certain; then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste;	And when recognized, a dislocation occurs when it moves towards the shoulder blade, and there's a clear distinction between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find their obvious difference.
et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens;	And you will find a hollow at the head of the shoulder. Also, from the shoulder blade to the elbow, it's like the shape of an 'O' for the diseased shoulder, and the patient can't bring their hand up to their nose, nor move it with any movements;
et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier;	And similarly, if it is dislocated upwards but not completely hidden, you will find it clearly at the elbow.
et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And this way of dislocation cannot remain unless it is new or if the child is ill.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And this method is that the minister lifts the hand away from the ill part at the top, then places his thumbs on the joint and raises the joint to force up at its place; and the minister lifts the hand and extends it upwards, putting it back in position; if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree;	And if it does not come as we have said on the third day, then the ill person should be bathed in warm water; and administer restorative and soothing treatments, such as decoctions of sage and fenugreek and clover herb, and make them into a wash.
puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide;	Then wrap the ill person's back with a piece of cloth, and place an evenly soft layer of wool under the joint, neither too soft nor too hard. Then place the heel on top of the layer, and lift the shoulder blade upwards in a virtuous manner, and pull the hand away from the illness.
et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere:	And another medical minister cuts the head of the limb, so that it does not move downwards; this shoulder comes back immediately, and if you see him to reset according to this manner:
et est que tu faices estre present .i. home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar;	And make sure the place where he stays is bigger than the limb; and it faces towards the body side, and pushes the shoulder up against the socket of the limb, and lifts the socket upwards, so that the limb hangs down in an arc;
et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre. Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And another medical minister pulls the hand of the limb downwards towards the belly. And if the limb is too light, then place something heavy with it, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche .i. lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com .i. pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile;	And you can also reset it in another way: and let's say you stick a long stick into the ground, such that the head is as wide as a bullet, and neither too large nor too slender;
puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment;	Place something under the hair but ensure it is covered with a skin membrane and let the hair remain as long as the rod. Then extend your hand downward from another side in form, and the joint will return to its place quickly.
et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren .i. tison de .ij. bras de grant et .iiij. dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And if it doesn't return due to all these things that we have mentioned, do this treatment: take one tournedavain of two large arms and three sticks of the same size, which has a head wide enough to enter smoothly from the front on both sides according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then tie it on the end of the rod covered with skin underneath, so that the rod does not hurt the hair, then place it against the skin from where you are to enter smoothly all around; and extend your arm along the rod from head to toe, and tie the shoulder on the rod, and the arm at the wrist, then put the arm on one of two long sticks about as wide, and keep the hand extended downward, and leave the body hanging from another side: the joint will return immediately now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is thus, in whatever way it may be, if need be you should put on the saddle a thread that's even, then place the plastered substance with mill-ground powder, along with incense and egg yolk, over the whole shoulder and around it, then remove from the saddle addition, and tie up the bandage onto the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let the hands remain in such a way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	It is necessary that he eats moderately, until the limbs are reinforced, for it will heal faster; and then eat more after five days or seven, and move them; and if it's firm and not softened, it is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a iij. pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is loose due to moisture that caused it or for another reason, you should administer four fires of the cautery, as was described in the section on cauteries previously.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all of this, and it dislocates after seven days, and the joint doesn't hold, and cannot lift your arm up, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is either cut or stretched or weakened; and know that the joint would never be fixed in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations in the buttocks area and breasts or rearward, are caused by pushing and stretching of hands, and performed at other locations; and treat until they heal properly.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after the healing comes redness to the limb, and persistent movements, then use hot baths many times, until that redness disappears and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	Know that the joint of the shoulder has been dislocated at its points, and returns to them; and if it's dislocated from all sides, as well as in front and behind, and dislocations are not responsive because one can see and feel them clearly; and is dislocated according to each figure.

And when you join the shoulder bone with the healthy part, if it's possible to see clearly. For the joint is hairy, and cannot bend the arm or touch its shoulder in any way.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it in such a way that the abscesses are closed and heal, for if they were left open, there would be complaint about having to bring them back; and sometimes they cannot be brought back completely, especially when they are at the back; it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and by chance death comes.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And this restoration is so done when it can be brought about that you extend its hand to your two hands; and its arms are spread out, and the hands are placed in front of you according to the line of the elbow, forward and backward, and hold the joint together with its elbows joined or at the base of its palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it will return when it doubles its hand to its hand, and raises the bone from the base of the palm that is dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large;	And if it does not wish to return to its place, administer strong extension; and if both hands extend the arm, and hold them together, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from each side, then once you have wrapped a long and wide double sheet around it;
et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne;	And when you touch the joint with your hand to join it together, if you apply some oil to soften the joint, then firmly set the joint back in place, until it heals.
et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie. Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in place, release the bandage, and leave it; and if you notice that the joint does not heal well, reapply the plaster and the bandage, and keep it this way for some days until it is firmly set; then remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse .i. jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain;	And if it feels painful after repositioning the joint, and it moves again, bathe it and scrub beautifully, pressing until it is relieved; or you can place a piece of fatty lamb skin on the joint, then leave it for one day and a night, then apply heat, and have them take a bath.
et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai .ij. fois ou .iij., tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And when he sweats, rub the joint in a timely manner, then place the ice back on it, and afterwards soak or bathe. And thus do this procedure either twice or three times, until he feels better; and if you see that improvement, apply moist cow's milk heated with butter to it, and rub it in; so that it will return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The hand dislocation occurs and the recovery is gentle, more so than other joints. Always bring it back to its place immediately upon dislocation, while in the same state as when it was dislocated, so that the limbs are swollen or an abscess arises.

And the resetting process involves placing your hand on the patient's side on a table, extending their arm out, and aligning them so that they match perfectly, thus having their palm placed against the appearance of the joint, and holding it until it resets.
Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	Otherwise, you must check if it is correctly in place; then have the patient support their hand's back on a table during extension and retraction.

Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If not, apply plaster casts for abscess drainage and leave them as such without repeating the process.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte;	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back into place after several days, then the joint remains twisted;
et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	and does not harm the patient as long as his limbs are immobilized, and cannot strain anything at all: then you know that the nerve is cut, or the artery; if there is no other way except to strain by cautery until the situation allows, and perhaps it has no other remedy.

des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the hip
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier. Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu;	And the knowledge of internal dislocation is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it is longer, and the diseased knee opens more than the healthy one, and the diseased knee cannot bend behind the joint.
et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And it is the limbs that are swollen from abscesses, because the head of the thigh bone comes into contact with them.

The understanding of this appearance of dislocation is that you should confirm if the dislocation is old and remains in its position, without any treatment; and there should be no assumption about it.

Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it should be extended immediately as I have said; and place their pain on the affected arm, then press with the other hand, and extend down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les .ij. hainches;	And if the dislocation is at the front, it does not suit to extend the patient's head backwardly, nor to lift them up from the ground, rather, it should be like when their hip was dislocated forwardly, as we have said about lying on both hips.
et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table;	and so on her face, and let the ligament stretch as we have said previously, and one should press at the joint to the table;
et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve;	and it will be correct when the patient's legs stretch and they are equal; then adjust the thighs, and apply the plaster, and tighten with a bandage so that the hip does not move.
et se repose .iij. jors ou .iiij., puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse. iij. jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and let them rest for three or four days, then release the bandage and place the plaster again; and if you see that they are equal, tighten it as before and leave it for three more days; then release the patient's movement gradually, until the limb is strengthened.
de la dislocation dou genoil	From shoulder joint dislocation
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The shoulders can be dislocated in three ways: this is to say, internally and externally, and behind; and they do not dislocate forward.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez;	And the signs for this are that you instruct the patient to bend their leg at their knee, and if they cannot bend it up to their knee, you know that their shoulder is dislocated.
et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez;	And for the restoration of all this, you should make the patient lie straight, and extend their leg if they can, and place your back against their buttocks, and put their foot on your feet;
puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les .ij. costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement;	Then take his knee in your palms, and draw it between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee joint. And some other servants extend his foot as far as the knee returns to its place, and the signs are that he has moved his leg lightly towards his thigh.
et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort .iij. jors ou iiij., puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	and place the dressing on it, and have him lift his leg to his thigh, and keep them together strongly for three or four days, then release him; and do not disturb the wounds of the leg until the limbs are strengthened.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limbs are not yet right, administer strong extension as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is cured.
de la dislocation dou talon	From the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes misaligned and not fully dislocated, both inside and outside.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee:	And the signs of this are that the ankle swells, and stretches forward towards the part where it is dislocated:
li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	The reduction should be done quickly; when the ankle is misaligned, you should gently extend it with your hands only if it's out of place.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne .i. ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville;	And when it is dislocated from the very beginning, it must be that you make the patient lie straight, and hold them up with two attendants by their leg, above the ankle;
puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre .ij. fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut;	then pull the foot towards you with your right hand, and then to your left hand twice, then lift them high, and hold the leg up firmly;
et fai ce .ij. fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient;	and do this twice, as we have said, pulling and moving the leg; if it returns, that is well; if not, start the process again, for it will return.
et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche .i. passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide;	and if it cannot return in this manner, then have the patient lie on their back on the ground, and stick one post firmly into the ground between their buttocks, and tie a cloth around them so as not to bruise the leg.
puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a .i. liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet;	Then have your attendants soak his chest in the broth, and some other servants extend one of their hands under his feet or at his waist, he ties onto the neck of the foot;
puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent;	Then extend all your attendants evenly, and have the sack placed firmly between the chest of the patient so that it can hold the patient when extended.
puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	Then position both eyes evenly on his shoulders, and have some other attendants soak the healthy leg at the knee, and the dislocated shoulder will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois;	And when it is at the right temperature, place the plaster and wrap it around firmly, then tie the leg to the thigh, and guard the nerves that are on the ankle behind, making sure the bandage isn't too tight.
puis le laisse .ij. jors ou .iij., et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par .iiij. jors;	Then let it be for two days or three, and if the bandage is removed, then pull on him; then release him on the third day or quarter of a day, and instruct him to move about for four more days;
et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And even if it goes beyond that point, it is not certain that it will not dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pus-filled areas have come out, you should soothe them as we have said elsewhere, until they are cleansed.
des dois	From these two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two shoulders are dislocated, if they suit to be beautifully extended in work, and it is a slight matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus .i. leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne;	And if the dislocations are not in any knot of the back or stone, it is necessary that you make the patient sit on his full length or on a table entirely straight, and place your foot where the joints spread, then press with your foot firmly until they come back into position.
et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a .ij. chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse .iij. jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when they are even and do not open anything, place one of your feet on a table with both shoulders, then press firmly, and leave him for three days, then release him; and let him rest until he recovers.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	On surgery and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert:	When injury comes with the dislocation, and one wishes to restore it, many times death occurs to the patient:
si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis;	if you are not modest in your treatment, and if you do not possess knowledge of the art and have not practiced it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and patient, then do not be rash.
et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit;	and in the beginning apply soothing treatments to the wound, and leave the patient in God's hands, if you do not see hope for recovery;
et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne;	And when you see hope, immediately reset the member at its place, so that the pus and wound drain out.
et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis;	And when the limb is at its place, administer remedies for pus drainage, and treat the wound accordingly, using dried ointments.
et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples;	And if it involves dislocation with fracture, and small bones are exposed, set the bones, and do as we have said for simple diseases.
et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors. Amen	And guard against entering paths of fear as I have said, for this befits you according to your Creator, and through knowledge and skill in treating yourself and your body. Amen.
Explicit le romen de fisique	Let the body's metabolism take its course
